# Amazon Listing Optimizer SaaS
## Complete Documentation Suite

**Version:** 1.0  
**Last Updated:** 2026-05-30  
**Status:** MVP Ready for Development  

---

## Project Overview

Amazon Listing Optimizer, health/supplements ve beauty kategorisinde Amazon'da satış yapan private label markalar için AI-destekli bir listing optimizasyon SaaS platformudur. Amazon'un COSMO (Common Sense Knowledge Graph) ve Rufus (Conversational AI Shopping Assistant) sistemlerini analiz ederek, satıcıların listing'lerini bu AI sistemlere göre optimize etmelerine yardımcı olur.

### Key Differentiators
- **AI-Native:** Semantic meaning ve user intent alignment (keyword stuffing değil)
- **Rufus Compatibility Score:** Listing'in Amazon AI'siyle ne kadar uyumlu olduğunu 0-100 skorla gösterir
- **Semantic Gap Analysis:** 24 boyutta eksiklik analizi ve önceliklendirme
- **COSMO Optimized:** Amazon'un knowledge graph ilişkilerine göre optimize edilmiş içerik üretir

---

---

## Quick Reference

### Technology Stack

```
Frontend:     React 19 + TypeScript + Vite + Tailwind CSS + shadcn/ui
Backend:      Hono + tRPC 11 + Drizzle ORM + Zod
Database:     MySQL 8.0 + Qdrant (Vector DB)
AI/ML:        OpenAI text-embedding-3-small (1536-dim)
Auth:         Kimi OAuth 2.0 + JWT Sessions
Payments:     Paddle (Subscriptions)
Hosting:      Hetzner VPS (CPX31) + Docker
Monitoring:   Sentry + Grafana + Prometheus
```

## Development Timeline

### Phase 1: Foundation (Weeks 1-2)
- [ ] VPS setup + Docker configuration
- [ ] Frontend + Backend initialization
- [ ] Database schema + migrations
- [ ] Authentication (Kimi OAuth)

### Phase 2: Core Features (Weeks 3-5)
- [ ] Amazon SP-API OAuth integration
- [ ] ASIN fetch + listing display
- [ ] OpenAI embedding integration
- [ ] Semantic gap analysis algorithm
- [ ] Rufus Compatibility Score
- [ ] Optimized title + bullets generation

### Phase 3: Polish (Weeks 6-7)
- [ ] Competitor benchmark
- [ ] Q&A optimization
- [ ] Paddle payment integration
- [ ] Subscription management
- [ ] UI/UX refinement

### Phase 4: Launch (Week 8+)
- [ ] Production deployment
- [ ] Monitoring setup
- [ ] Beta testing
- [ ] Product Hunt launch
- [ ] Marketing push

## Cost Breakdown

### Development Costs

| Item | Cost | Notes |
|------|------|-------|
| VPS (Hetzner CPX31) | $33/month | 8 vCPU, 32 GB RAM |
| Domain | $10/year | Namecheap/Cloudflare |
| OpenAI API | $2-5/month | Embedding costs |
| Paddle | 5% commission | On successful payments |
| Sentry (Free tier) | $0 | 5,000 errors/month |
| **Total Monthly** | **~$40-50** | MVP operational cost |

### Revenue Projections

| Metric | Month 1 | Month 3 | Month 6 | Month 12 |
|--------|---------|---------|---------|----------|
| Users | 50 | 200 | 500 | 1,500 |
| Paid Users (20%) | 10 | 40 | 100 | 300 |
| MRR | $500 | $3,000 | $7,500 | $22,500 |
| Monthly Profit | $450 | $2,950 | $7,450 | $22,450 |

     8	// Allow custom DB path via environment variable (essential for VPS deployments to persist data outside the code directory)
     9	const bundledDbPath = process.env.DB_PATH
    10	  ? path.resolve(process.env.DB_PATH)
    11	  : path.resolve(__dirname, "../../data/optimus.db");

    13	const isVercel = !!process.env.VERCEL;
    14	
    15	/**
    16	 * On Vercel, the bundled DB file is inside the read-only deployment bundle.
    17	 * We copy it to /tmp (the only writable directory in a serverless function)
    18	 * so that mutation endpoints (bookings, views, activities) can write.
    19	 * 
    20	 * ⚠️ CRITICAL: /tmp is ephemeral — data does not persist across cold starts.
    21	 * All writes (prospects, bookings, activities, pipeline jobs) are LOST when
    22	 * the function instance recycles. For production persistence, migrate to:
    23	 *   - PostgreSQL (Neon, Supabase, Railway)
    24	 *   - MySQL (PlanetScale, RDS)
    25	 *   - Or use Vercel Postgres / Vercel Blob for specific data
    26	 * 
    27	 * This SQLite setup is suitable for demos and local development only.
    28	 */
    29	let dbPath: string;
    30	
    31	if (isVercel) {
    32	  const tmpDbPath = "/tmp/optimus.db";
    33	  if (!fs.existsSync(tmpDbPath) && fs.existsSync(bundledDbPath)) {
    34	    fs.copyFileSync(bundledDbPath, tmpDbPath);
    35	    console.log(`📋 Copied bundled DB to writable /tmp for Vercel.`);
    36	  }
    37	  dbPath = tmpDbPath;
    38	} else {
    39	  dbPath = bundledDbPath;

   255	/**
   256	 * Execute a function within an explicit SQLite transaction.
   257	 * Automatically commits on success, rolls back on error.
   258	 */
   259	export function withTransaction<T>(fn: (db: Database.Database) => T): T {
   260	  db.prepare("BEGIN").run();
   261	  try {
   262	    const result = fn(db);
   263	    db.prepare("COMMIT").run();
   264	    return result;
   265	  } catch (err) {
   266	    db.prepare("ROLLBACK").run();
   267	    throw err;
   268	  }
   269	}
   270	
   271	export async function withTransactionAsync<T>(
   272	  fn: (db: Database.Database) => Promise<T>
   273	): Promise<T> {
   274	  db.prepare("BEGIN").run();
   275	  try {
   276	    const result = await fn(db);
   277	    db.prepare("COMMIT").run();
   278	    return result;
   279	  } catch (err) {
   280	    db.prepare("ROLLBACK").run();
   281	    throw err;
   282	  }
   283	}

<details><summary>Tool Result: ReadFile (`api/services/llmGateway.ts`)</summary>

<!-- call_id: tool_gnmZ1urM0pOOG3EJktexlGLh -->

     1	import { getCircuitBreaker } from "./circuitBreaker.js";
     2	import { tokenBudgetService } from "./tokenBudget.js";
     3	import { logger } from "../infra/logger.js";
     4	import { eventBus } from "../infra/eventBus.js";
     5	
     6	const OPENAI_API_KEY = process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY;
     7	const OPENROUTER_API_KEY = process.env.OPENROUTER_API_KEY;
     8	const OPENROUTER_MODEL = process.env.OPENROUTER_MODEL || "openai/gpt-4o-mini";
     9	
    10	interface LlmRequest {
    11	  model?: string;
    12	  messages: Array<{ role: string; content: string }>;
    13	  temperature?: number;
    14	  max_tokens?: number;
    15	  response_format?: { type: string };
    16	}
    17	
    18	interface LlmResponse {
    19	  content: string;
    20	  promptTokens: number;
    21	  completionTokens: number;
    22	  totalTokens: number;
    23	}
    24	
    25	interface LlmCallOptions {
    26	  prospectId: number;
    27	  jobId?: number;
    28	  service: string;
    29	  estimatedCostCents: number;
    30	  correlationId?: string;
    31	}
    32	
    33	/**
    34	 * Centralized LLM gateway that wraps all OpenAI/OpenRouter calls with:
    35	 * - Token budget checking
    36	 * - Circuit breaker protection
    37	 * - Usage tracking
    38	 * - Structured logging & events
    39	 */
    40	export async function callLlm(
    41	  request: LlmRequest,
    42	  options: LlmCallOptions
    43	): Promise<LlmResponse> {
    44	  // 1. Budget check
    45	  tokenBudgetService.checkBudget(options.prospectId, options.estimatedCostCents);
    46	
    47	  // 2. Circuit breaker
    48	  const breaker = getCircuitBreaker("llm-gateway");
    49	
    50	  return breaker.execute(async () => {
    51	    logger.info(`LLM request started`, {
    52	      service: options.service,
    53	      prospectId: options.prospectId,
    54	      jobId: options.jobId,
    55	      correlationId: options.correlationId,
    56	    });
    57	
    58	    eventBus.emit(
    59	      "llm:request",
    60	      { service: options.service, model: request.model, maxTokens: request.max_tokens },
    61	      options.correlationId
    62	    );
    63	
    64	    const url = OPENROUTER_API_KEY
    65	      ? "https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions"
    66	      : "https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions";
    67	    const apiKey = OPENROUTER_API_KEY || OPENAI_API_KEY;
    68	    const model = request.model ?? (OPENROUTER_API_KEY ? OPENROUTER_MODEL : "gpt-4o-mini");
    69	
    70	    if (!apiKey) {
    71	      throw new Error("No LLM API key configured (OPENAI_API_KEY or OPENROUTER_API_KEY)");
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    const headers: Record<string, string> = {
    75	      "Content-Type": "application/json",
    76	      Authorization: `Bearer ${apiKey}`,
    77	    };
    78	
    79	    if (OPENROUTER_API_KEY) {
    80	      headers["HTTP-Referer"] = "https://github.com/ymehmetdemiroglu-crypto/optius-rufus";
    81	      headers["X-Title"] = "Optimus Rufus";
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    const response = await fetch(url, {
    85	      method: "POST",
    86	      headers,
    87	      body: JSON.stringify({
    88	        model,
    89	        messages: request.messages,
    90	        temperature: request.temperature ?? 0.7,
    91	        max_tokens: request.max_tokens ?? 2000,
    92	        response_format: request.response_format,
    93	      }),
    94	    });
    95	
    96	    if (!response.ok) {
    97	      const text = await response.text();
    98	      throw new Error(`LLM API error ${response.status}: ${text}`);
    99	    }
   100	
   101	    const data = (await response.json()) as {
   102	      choices: Array<{ message: { content: string } }>;
   103	      usage?: { prompt_tokens: number; completion_tokens: number; total_tokens: number };
   104	    };
   105	
   106	    const content = data.choices[0]?.message?.content ?? "";
   107	    const promptTokens = data.usage?.prompt_tokens ?? 0;
   108	    const completionTokens = data.usage?.completion_tokens ?? 0;
   109	    const totalTokens = data.usage?.total_tokens ?? promptTokens + completionTokens;
   110	
   111	    // Estimate cost: $0.0015 per 1K tokens for gpt-4o-mini (very rough)
   112	    const costCents = Math.ceil((totalTokens / 1000) * 0.15);
   113	
   114	    // Track usage
   115	    tokenBudgetService.trackUsage(
   116	      options.prospectId,
   117	      options.jobId,
   118	      options.service,
   119	      promptTokens,
   120	      completionTokens,
   121	      costCents
   122	    );
   123	
   124	    logger.info(`LLM request completed`, {
   125	      service: options.service,
   126	      prospectId: options.prospectId,
   127	      jobId: options.jobId,
   128	      totalTokens,
   129	      costCents,
   130	      correlationId: options.correlationId,
   131	    });
   132	
   133	    eventBus.emit(
   134	      "llm:success",
   135	      { service: options.service, totalTokens, costCents },
   136	      options.correlationId
   137	    );
   138	
   139	    return {
   140	      content,
   141	      promptTokens,
   142	      completionTokens,
   143	      totalTokens,
   144	    };
   145	  });
   146	}

<details><summary>Tool Result: ReadFile (`api/pipeline/worker.ts`)</summary>

<!-- call_id: tool_ZwKq7Ut4LdiUx7OtxuGSvJMd -->
<system>86 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 86. End of file reached.</system>
     1	import { pipelineQueue } from "../infra/queue.js";
     2	import { logger } from "../infra/logger.js";
     3	import { pipelineEngine } from "./engine.js";
     4	import type { Job } from "../infra/types.js";
     5	
     6	/**
     7	 * QueueWorker polls the SQLite job queue and processes pipeline jobs.
     8	 * In a serverless environment, this should be triggered by a cron or
     9	 * external scheduler. In a long-running process (PM2/VPS), start() runs
    10	 * a continuous polling loop.
    11	 */
    12	export class QueueWorker {
    13	  private running = false;
    14	  private timer?: NodeJS.Timeout;
    15	  private readonly pollIntervalMs: number;
    16	
    17	  constructor(pollIntervalMs = 2000) {
    18	    this.pollIntervalMs = pollIntervalMs;
    19	  }
    20	
    21	  /**
    22	   * Process a single job from the queue.
    23	   * Returns true if a job was processed, false if queue is empty.
    24	   */
    25	  async processOne(): Promise<boolean> {
    26	    const job = pipelineQueue.pollNext();
    27	    if (!job) return false;
    28	
    29	    pipelineQueue.markActive(job.id);
    30	    logger.info(`Processing job ${job.id} (${job.name})`, { jobId: job.id });
    31	
    32	    try {
    33	      if (job.name === "run-pipeline") {
    34	        const data = job.data as { jobId: number; correlationId: string; retryStage?: string };
    35	        await pipelineEngine.runJob(data.jobId, data.correlationId);
    36	      } else {
    37	        throw new Error(`Unknown job name: ${job.name}`);
    38	      }
    39	
    40	      pipelineQueue.markCompleted(job.id, { success: true });
    41	      logger.info(`Job ${job.id} completed`, { jobId: job.id });
    42	      return true;
    43	    } catch (err) {
    44	      const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
    45	      const stack = err instanceof Error ? err.stack ?? "" : "";
    46	      pipelineQueue.markFailed(job.id, message, stack ? [stack] : []);
    47	      logger.error(`Job ${job.id} failed`, { jobId: job.id, error: message });
    48	      return true;
    49	    }
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  /**
    53	   * Start continuous polling loop.
    54	   */
    55	  start(): void {
    56	    if (this.running) return;
    57	    this.running = true;
    58	    logger.info("QueueWorker started", { intervalMs: this.pollIntervalMs });
    59	
    60	    const tick = async () => {
    61	      if (!this.running) return;
    62	      try {
    63	        const hadWork = await this.processOne();
    64	        // If work was found, process again immediately; otherwise wait
    65	        this.timer = setTimeout(tick, hadWork ? 0 : this.pollIntervalMs);
    66	      } catch (err) {
    67	        logger.error("QueueWorker tick error", { error: String(err) });
    68	        this.timer = setTimeout(tick, this.pollIntervalMs);
    69	      }
    70	    };
    71	
    72	    tick();
    73	  }
    74	
    75	  /**
    76	   * Stop the polling loop.
    77	   */
    78	  stop(): void {
    79	    this.running = false;
    80	    if (this.timer) clearTimeout(this.timer);
    81	    logger.info("QueueWorker stopped");
    82	  }
    83	}
    84	
    85	// Singleton worker instance
    86	export const queueWorker = new QueueWorker();


</details>

<details><summary>Tool Result: ReadFile (`api/pipeline/engine.ts`)</summary>

<!-- call_id: tool_WM6x2fwQkqJyBt624Mpj20PE -->

     1	import { db, withTransaction } from "../db/client.js";
     2	import { eventBus } from "../infra/eventBus.js";
     3	import { logger } from "../infra/logger.js";
     4	import { pipelineQueue } from "../infra/queue.js";
     5	import type { PipelineJob, StageName, StageOutput, StageContext } from "./types.js";
     6	import { STAGE_ORDER, stageExecutors } from "./stages.js";
     7	
     8	function safeJson<T>(text: string | undefined | null, fallback: T): T {
     9	  if (!text) return fallback;
    10	  try {
    11	    return JSON.parse(text) as T;
    12	  } catch {
    13	    return fallback;
    14	  }
    15	}
    16	
    17	export class PipelineEngine {
    18	  /**
    19	   * Insert pipeline job and stage rows into DB.
    20	   */
    21	  private insertJob(
    22	    prospectId: number,
    23	    listingId: number | undefined,
    24	    packageType: string
    25	  ): { jobId: number; correlationId: string } {
    26	    const correlationId = `job-${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 7)}`;
    27	
    28	    const result = db
    29	      .prepare(
    30	        `INSERT INTO pipeline_jobs (prospectId, listingId, packageType, status, stagesJSON)
    31	         VALUES (?, ?, ?, 'pending', '{}')`
    32	      )
    33	      .run(prospectId, listingId ?? null, packageType);
    34	
    35	    const jobId = Number(result.lastInsertRowid);
    36	
    37	    // Initialize stage rows
    38	    const insertStage = db.prepare(
    39	      `INSERT INTO pipeline_job_stages (jobId, stageName, status)
    40	       VALUES (?, ?, 'pending')`
    41	    );
    42	    for (const stage of STAGE_ORDER) {
    43	      insertStage.run(jobId, stage.name);
    44	    }
    45	
    46	    logger.info(`Pipeline job created`, { jobId, prospectId, packageType, correlationId });
    47	    eventBus.emit("pipeline:created", { jobId, prospectId, packageType }, String(correlationId));
    48	
    49	    return { jobId, correlationId };
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  /**
    53	   * Create a new pipeline job and enqueue it for async processing.
    54	   */
    55	  async createJob(
    56	    prospectId: number,
    57	    listingId: number | undefined,
    58	    packageType: string
    59	  ): Promise<{ jobId: number }> {
    60	    const { jobId, correlationId } = this.insertJob(prospectId, listingId, packageType);
    61	    await pipelineQueue.add("run-pipeline", { jobId, correlationId });
    62	    return { jobId };
    63	  }
    64	
    65	  /**
    66	   * Create and run a pipeline job synchronously (for backward-compatible routes).
    67	   */
    68	  async createAndRunJob(
    69	    prospectId: number,
    70	    listingId: number | undefined,
    71	    packageType: string
    72	  ): Promise<PipelineJob> {
    73	    const { jobId, correlationId } = this.insertJob(prospectId, listingId, packageType);
    74	    await this.runJob(jobId, correlationId);
    75	    const job = this.getJob(jobId);
    76	    if (!job) throw new Error(`Pipeline job ${jobId} disappeared after run`);
    77	    return job;
    78	  }
    79	
    80	  /**
    81	   * Get the current state of a pipeline job.
    82	   */
    83	  getJob(jobId: number): PipelineJob | null {
    84	    const row = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM pipeline_jobs WHERE id = ?").get(jobId) as
    85	      | Record<string, unknown>
    86	      | undefined;
    87	    if (!row) return null;
    88	
    89	    const stageRows = db
    90	      .prepare("SELECT * FROM pipeline_job_stages WHERE jobId = ?")
    91	      .all(jobId) as Array<Record<string, unknown>>;
    92	
    93	    const stages: PipelineJob["stages"] = {} as PipelineJob["stages"];
    94	    for (const sr of stageRows) {
    95	      stages[sr.stageName as StageName] = {
    96	        status: sr.status as PipelineJob["stages"][StageName]["status"],
    97	        output: sr.outputJSON ? safeJson(String(sr.outputJSON), undefined) : undefined,
    98	        errorMessage: sr.errorMessage ? String(sr.errorMessage) : undefined,
    99	        startedAt: sr.startedAt ? String(sr.startedAt) : undefined,
   100	        completedAt: sr.completedAt ? String(sr.completedAt) : undefined,
   101	      };
   102	    }
   103	
   104	    return {
   105	      id: Number(row.id),
   106	      prospectId: Number(row.prospectId),
   107	      listingId: row.listingId ? Number(row.listingId) : undefined,
   108	      packageType: String(row.packageType),
   109	      status: String(row.status) as PipelineJob["status"],
   110	      currentStage: row.currentStage ? String(row.currentStage) as StageName : undefined,
   111	      stages,
   112	      tokenUsage: Number(row.tokenUsage ?? 0),
   113	      errorLog: row.errorLog ? String(row.errorLog) : undefined,
   114	      createdAt: String(row.createdAt),
   115	      updatedAt: String(row.updatedAt),
   116	    };
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  /**
   120	   * Run (or resume) a pipeline job.
   121	   */
   122	  async runJob(jobId: number, correlationId: string): Promise<void> {
   123	    const job = this.getJob(jobId);
   124	    if (!job) {
   125	      throw new Error(`Pipeline job ${jobId} not found`);
   126	    }
   127	
   128	    logger.info(`Pipeline run starting`, { jobId, correlationId });
   129	    eventBus.emit("pipeline:start", { jobId }, String(correlationId));
   130	
   131	    db.prepare("UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET status = 'running', updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?")
   132	      .run(jobId);
   133	
   134	    try {
   135	      const stageOutputs: StageOutput = {};
   136	
   137	      for (const stageDef of STAGE_ORDER) {
   138	        const stageState = job.stages[stageDef.name];
   139	
   140	        // Skip already completed stages, but load their output
   141	        if (stageState.status === "completed" && stageState.output) {
   142	          (stageOutputs as Record<string, unknown>)[stageDef.name] = stageState.output;
   143	          continue;
   144	        }
   145	
   146	        // Check dependencies
   147	        const missingDeps = stageDef.dependencies.filter(
   148	          (dep) => !stageOutputs[dep] && job.stages[dep]?.status !== "completed"
   149	        );
   150	        if (missingDeps.length > 0) {
   151	          throw new Error(
   152	            `Stage ${stageDef.name} cannot run: missing dependencies [${missingDeps.join(", ")}]`
   153	          );
   154	        }
   155	
   156	        // Mark stage as running
   157	        db.prepare(
   158	          `UPDATE pipeline_job_stages
   159	           SET status = 'running', startedAt = datetime('now')
   160	           WHERE jobId = ? AND stageName = ?`
   161	        ).run(jobId, stageDef.name);
   162	
   163	        db.prepare(
   164	          `UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET currentStage = ?, updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?`
   165	        ).run(stageDef.name, jobId);
   166	
   167	        const executor = stageExecutors.find((e) => e.name === stageDef.name);
   168	        if (!executor) {
   169	          throw new Error(`No executor found for stage ${stageDef.name}`);
   170	        }
   171	
   172	        const ctx: StageContext = {
   173	          jobId,
   174	          prospectId: job.prospectId,
   175	          packageType: job.packageType,
   176	          correlationId,
   177	          stageOutputs,
   178	        };
   179	
   180	        try {
   181	          const output = await executor.execute(ctx);
   182	          (stageOutputs as Record<string, unknown>)[stageDef.name] = output;
   183	
   184	          // Persist stage completion
   185	          db.prepare(
   186	            `UPDATE pipeline_job_stages
   187	             SET status = 'completed', outputJSON = ?, completedAt = datetime('now')
   188	             WHERE jobId = ? AND stageName = ?`
   189	          ).run(JSON.stringify(output), jobId, stageDef.name);
   190	        } catch (stageErr) {
   191	          const message = stageErr instanceof Error ? stageErr.message : String(stageErr);
   192	
   193	          db.prepare(
   194	            `UPDATE pipeline_job_stages
   195	             SET status = 'failed', errorMessage = ?
   196	             WHERE jobId = ? AND stageName = ?`
   197	          ).run(message, jobId, stageDef.name);
   198	
   199	          db.prepare(
   200	            `UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET status = 'failed', errorLog = ?, updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?`
   201	          ).run(message, jobId);
   202	
   203	          logger.error(`Pipeline stage failed`, {
   204	            jobId,
   205	            stage: stageDef.name,
   206	            error: message,
   207	            correlationId,
   208	          });
   209	          eventBus.emit("pipeline:error", { jobId, stage: stageDef.name, error: message }, String(correlationId));
   210	          return;
   211	        }
   212	      }
   213	
   214	      // All stages completed
   215	      db.prepare(
   216	        `UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET status = 'completed', currentStage = NULL, updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?`
   217	      ).run(jobId);
   218	
   219	      logger.info(`Pipeline completed`, { jobId, correlationId });
   220	      eventBus.emit("pipeline:complete", { jobId }, String(correlationId));
   221	    } catch (err) {
   222	      const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
   223	      db.prepare(
   224	        `UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET status = 'failed', errorLog = ?, updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?`
   225	      ).run(message, jobId);
   226	
   227	      logger.error(`Pipeline failed`, { jobId, error: message, correlationId });
   228	      eventBus.emit("pipeline:error", { jobId, error: message }, String(correlationId));
   229	    }
   230	  }
   231	
   232	  /**
   233	   * Retry a specific failed stage.
   234	   */
   235	  async retryStage(jobId: number, stageName: StageName): Promise<void> {
   236	    const job = this.getJob(jobId);
   237	    if (!job) throw new Error(`Job ${jobId} not found`);
   238	
   239	    const correlationId = `retry-${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 7)}`;
   240	
   241	    db.prepare(
   242	      `UPDATE pipeline_job_stages SET status = 'pending', errorMessage = NULL WHERE jobId = ? AND stageName = ?`
   243	    ).run(jobId, stageName);
   244	
   245	    db.prepare(
   246	      `UPDATE pipeline_jobs SET status = 'pending', errorLog = NULL, updatedAt = datetime('now') WHERE id = ?`
   247	    ).run(jobId);
   248	
   249	    await pipelineQueue.add("run-pipeline", { jobId, correlationId, retryStage: stageName });
   250	
   251	    logger.info(`Stage retry enqueued`, { jobId, stage: stageName, correlationId });
   252	    eventBus.emit("pipeline:retry", { jobId, stage: stageName }, String(correlationId));
   253	  }
   254	}
   255	
   256	export const pipelineEngine = new PipelineEngine();


</details>

import fs from "fs";
import path from "path";
import { fileURLToPath } from "url";
import { db } from "../client.js";

const __dirname = path.dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url));

interface MigrationRecord {
  id: number;
  filename: string;
  appliedAt: string;
}

export function initMigrations() {
  // Ensure migrations tracking table exists
  db.exec(`
    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_migrations (
      id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
      filename TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
      appliedAt DATETIME DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
    )
  `);

  // Get already applied migrations
  const appliedRows = db
    .prepare("SELECT filename FROM schema_migrations")
    .all() as MigrationRecord[];
  const applied = new Set(appliedRows.map((r) => r.filename));

  // Read migration files in order
  const files = fs
    .readdirSync(__dirname)
    .filter((f) => f.endsWith(".sql"))
    .sort();

  for (const filename of files) {
    if (applied.has(filename)) {
      continue;
    }

    const filepath = path.join(__dirname, filename);
    const sql = fs.readFileSync(filepath, "utf-8");

    console.log(`🔄 Running migration: ${filename}`);

    // Run migration inside a transaction
    const run = db.transaction(() => {
      db.exec(sql);
      db.prepare("INSERT INTO schema_migrations (filename) VALUES (?)").run(
        filename
      );
    });

    try {
      run();
      console.log(`✅ Migration applied: ${filename}`);
    } catch (err) {
      console.error(`❌ Migration failed: ${filename}`, err);
      throw err;
    }
  }
}

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the project. Let me synthesize my findings into the most important upgrade areas.

Key observations:
1. **Database**: The docs specify MySQL + Drizzle ORM + Qdrant vector DB, but the actual implementation uses raw SQLite (better-sqlite3) with handwritten SQL. No ORM, no vector DB. The SQLite setup on Vercel is explicitly noted as ephemeral.
2. **Dependencies**: tRPC is on an RC version (11.0.0-rc.362), React 19 is being used, but many other dependencies might be outdated. There's no testing framework.
3. **Auth**: The docs mention Kimi OAuth + JWT, but I haven't seen auth middleware or protected routes implemented. The .env has auth vars but no actual auth system visible.
4. **No Tests**: Zero test files in the project. No testing framework configured.
5. **Build/Deployment**: There's a .vercel directory suggesting deployment there, but the SQLite notes explicitly say data doesn't persist. No Dockerfile or docker-compose despite docs mentioning Docker.
6. **Type Safety**: The db client uses raw SQL with manual type casting. No Drizzle ORM as documented.
7. **Payments**: Paddle is documented but likely not implemented.
8. **Monitoring**: Sentry is documented but may not be integrated.
9. **Amazon SP-API**: Documented but may not be fully implemented.

Let me look at a couple more things to confirm my assessment.

import { Hono, type Context } from "hono";
import { cors } from "hono/cors";
import { fetchRequestHandler } from "@trpc/server/adapters/fetch";
import { appRouter } from "./router.js";
import "./db/schema.js";
import fs from "fs";
import path from "path";

import { generatePdf } from "./services/pdf.js";
import { pipelineSseHandler } from "./sse/pipeline.js";
import { queueWorker } from "./pipeline/worker.js";
import { db } from "./db/client.js";

export const app = new Hono();

// A simple serveStatic replacement using Node fs for portable and error-free execution
function serveStatic(options: { root?: string; path?: string }) {
  return async (c: Context, next: () => Promise<void>) => {
    let filePath = options.path;
    if (!filePath && options.root) {
      const urlPath = c.req.path;
      filePath = path.join(options.root, urlPath);
    }
    
    if (filePath && fs.existsSync(filePath) && fs.statSync(filePath).isFile()) {
      const content = fs.readFileSync(filePath);
      const ext = path.extname(filePath).toLowerCase();
      const mimeTypes: Record<string, string> = {
        ".html": "text/html",
        ".css": "text/css",
        ".js": "application/javascript",
        ".json": "application/json",
        ".png": "image/png",
        ".jpg": "image/jpeg",
        ".gif": "image/gif",
        ".svg": "image/svg+xml",
        ".ico": "image/x-icon",
      };
      c.header("Content-Type", mimeTypes[ext] || "application/octet-stream");
      return c.body(content);
    }
    await next();
  };
}

// CORS — restrict in production, allow all in development
const allowedOrigins = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGINS
  ? process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGINS.split(",").map((o) => o.trim())
  : process.env.NODE_ENV === "production"
    ? []
    : ["*"];

app.use("*", cors({
  origin: (origin) => {
    if (!origin) return origin;
    if (allowedOrigins.includes("*")) return origin;
    if (allowedOrigins.includes(origin)) return origin;
    return null;
  },
}));

// Health check with DB connectivity
app.get("/health", (c) => {
  try {
    db.prepare("SELECT 1").get();
    return c.json({ status: "ok", version: process.env.APP_VERSION || "1.0.0", db: "connected" });
  } catch {
    return c.json({ status: "degraded", version: process.env.APP_VERSION || "1.0.0", db: "disconnected" }, 503);
  }
});

// SSE pipeline progress streaming
app.get("/api/sse/pipeline/:jobId", (c) => pipelineSseHandler(c));

// PDF Download route
app.get("/api/pdf/:slug", async (c) => {
  const slug = c.req.param("slug");
  try {
    const pdfBuffer = await generatePdf(slug);
    c.header("Content-Type", "application/pdf");
    c.header("Content-Disposition", `attachment; filename="optimus-rufus-audit-${slug}.pdf"`);
    return c.body(pdfBuffer as any);
  } catch (err: any) {
    console.error("❌ [Hono] PDF download route failed:", err);
    return c.text(`Failed to generate PDF: ${err.message}`, 500);
  }
});

// tRPC API endpoint
app.use("/api/trpc/*", async (c) => {
  const response = await fetchRequestHandler({
    endpoint: "/api/trpc",
    req: c.req.raw,
    router: appRouter,
    createContext: () => ({}),
  });
  return response;
});

// Serve static frontend files in production
if (process.env.NODE_ENV === "production") {
  app.use("/*", serveStatic({ root: "./dist" }));
  app.get("*", serveStatic({ path: "./dist/index.html" }));
}

const port = parseInt(process.env.PORT || "3000", 10);

console.log(`🚀 Optimus Rufus server running on http://localhost:${port}`);

// Bun/Deno/Node compatibility

// Node native fetch server
import { createServer } from "http";

const httpServer = createServer(async (req, res) => {
  const url = new URL(req.url || "/", `http://${req.headers.host}`);
  const request = new Request(url, {
    method: req.method,
    headers: new Headers(
      Object.entries(req.headers).map(([k, v]) => [k, Array.isArray(v) ? v.join(", ") : v || ""]) as any
    ),
    // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
    body: (req.method !== "GET" && req.method !== "HEAD" ? await getBody(req) : undefined) as any,
  });

  const response = await app.fetch(request);

  res.statusCode = response.status;
  response.headers.forEach((value, key) => {
    res.setHeader(key, value);
  });

  if (response.body) {
    const reader = response.body.getReader();
    while (true) {
      const { done, value } = await reader.read();
      if (done) break;
      res.write(Buffer.from(value));
    }
  }
  res.end();
});

function getBody(req: import("http").IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {
  return new Promise((resolve) => {
    const chunks: Buffer[] = [];
    req.on("data", (chunk) => chunks.push(chunk));
    req.on("end", () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)));
  });
}

if (!process.env.VERCEL) {
  httpServer.listen(port, () => {
    console.log(`🚀 Server listening on http://localhost:${port}`);
    console.log(`📡 tRPC endpoint: http://localhost:${port}/api/trpc`);
    console.log(`📊 SSE endpoint: http://localhost:${port}/api/sse/pipeline/:jobId`);

    // Start background job worker for non-serverless environments
    queueWorker.start();
  });
}

    50	 * Converts our stub-style router objects to real tRPC routers.
    51	 * Stub objects have: { type: 'query'|'mutation', input: ZodSchema, resolve: fn }
    52	 */
    53	export function stubToRouter(stub: Record<string, unknown>) {
    54	  const converted: Record<string, unknown> = {};
    55	
    56	  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(stub)) {
    57	    if (value === null || typeof value !== "object") {
    58	      converted[key] = value;
    59	      continue;
    60	    }

    66	      if (v.input && v.input instanceof z.ZodType) {
    67	        converted[key] = proc.input(v.input as z.ZodTypeAny).query(v.resolve as any);
    68	      } else {
    69	        converted[key] = proc.query(v.resolve as any);
    70	      }
    71	    } else if (v.type === "mutation" && typeof v.resolve === "function") {

    76	        converted[key] = proc.mutation(v.resolve as any);
    77	      }
    78	    } else {
    79	      // Nested router object
    80	      converted[key] = stubToRouter(v as Record<string, unknown>);
    81	    }
    82	  }
    83	
    84	  return converted;

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the project. Let me synthesize the most important upgrade areas.

Key findings:
1. **Database Layer Mismatch**: Docs say MySQL + Drizzle ORM + Qdrant, but actual code uses raw SQLite with handwritten SQL. No ORM, no migrations as code, no type-safe queries.
2. **No Authentication System**: Docs mention Kimi OAuth + JWT, but the actual auth is just a stub optional API_KEY check. No real user sessions, no protected routes properly.
3. **Zero Testing**: No test files, no testing framework (Jest/Vitest/Playwright). 61 ESLint errors exist.
4. **Vercel SQLite Ephemeral Data**: The code explicitly acknowledges that on Vercel, SQLite data is lost on cold starts. No persistent DB for production.
5. **Missing Core Features**: No Paddle payments, no Sentry monitoring, no proper Amazon SP-API integration (just stubs/services).
6. **Type Safety Issues**: 61 ESLint errors, many `any` types, `setState` in effects anti-pattern.
7. **tRPC RC Version**: Using release candidate version of tRPC 11.
8. **No Docker/Deployment Config**: Docs mention Docker but no Dockerfile or docker-compose exists.

Let me organize these into the most impactful upgrade areas.

</details>

Based on my analysis of the codebase, docs, and configuration, here are the **most important areas to upgrade**, ranked by impact and urgency:

---

### 1. **Database Layer (Critical)**
Your docs specify **MySQL + Drizzle ORM + Qdrant**, but the actual implementation uses raw **SQLite with handwritten SQL strings**. This is the biggest architectural gap.

- **Why it matters**: No type-safe queries, no schema migrations as code, and on Vercel all writes are **ephemeral** (explicitly noted in `api/db/client.ts`: "data is lost on cold starts")
- **Upgrade path**: Adopt Drizzle ORM with PostgreSQL/MySQL (Neon, Supabase, or Railway) as documented. This gives you type-safe queries, proper migrations, and persistent production data.

---

### 2. **Authentication & Authorization (Critical)**
The docs promise **Kimi OAuth + JWT sessions**, but the actual `api/trpc.ts` shows only a stub optional `API_KEY` check with the comment *"Auth not configured — allow through (backward compatible)"*.

- **Why it matters**: Admin dashboard (`AdminDashboard.tsx`), prospect data, and booking endpoints are effectively unprotected. Anyone can hit your tRPC endpoints.
- **Upgrade path**: Implement real OAuth flow with JWT sessions, add `authProcedure` middleware, and protect sensitive mutations.

---

### 3. **Testing Infrastructure (High)**
**Zero tests exist**. No unit tests, no integration tests, no E2E tests. There isn't even a testing framework installed.

- **Why it matters**: You have 61 ESLint errors, complex async pipeline logic, and LLM-dependent services — all untested. Refactoring is risky.
- **Upgrade path**: Add **Vitest** for backend unit tests, **React Testing Library** for components, and **Playwright** for E2E flows (landing → pipeline → PDF download).

---

### 4. **Code Quality & Type Safety (High)**
Running `npm run lint` surfaces **61 errors**, mostly:
- `any` types throughout (`@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any`)
- `setState` called directly in `useEffect` (anti-pattern causing extra renders)
- Unused variables and dead assignments

- **Upgrade path**: Fix the `any` types (especially in tRPC context, DB queries, and pipeline stages), resolve the React hooks violations, and add a pre-commit hook (Husky + lint-staged) to prevent regressions.

---

### 5. **Production Deployment & Infrastructure (High)**
You're deployed on **Vercel with SQLite**, but the codebase itself warns this is "suitable for demos and local development only." Meanwhile, the docs mention **Docker on Hetzner VPS** — yet no `Dockerfile` or `docker-compose.yml` exists.

- **Why it matters**: Pipeline jobs, bookings, and prospect activities vanish when the function recycles.
- **Upgrade path**: Either add Vercel Postgres/Neon for persistence, or commit to the Docker + VPS path with a real `docker-compose.yml` for the app + MySQL + Qdrant.

---

### 6. **tRPC Version (Medium)**
You're on `11.0.0-rc.362` — a release candidate. tRPC v11 has since stabilized.

- **Upgrade path**: Bump to the stable `^11.0.0` release. This reduces risk of breaking changes and gives you proper upstream support.

---

### 7. **Missing Core Business Features (Medium)**
Several documented features appear to be stubs or entirely absent:
- **Paddle payments/subscriptions** — Not implemented
- **Sentry monitoring** — Env vars exist but no SDK integration visible
- **Amazon SP-API OAuth** — Services exist but integration may be incomplete
- **Qdrant vector search** — Embedding strings are stored in SQLite TEXT columns

---

### Summary Priority Matrix

| Priority | Area | Effort | Impact |
|----------|------|--------|--------|
| 🔴 P0 | Database (SQLite → PostgreSQL/MySQL + Drizzle) | High | Critical |
| 🔴 P0 | Authentication (OAuth + JWT) | Medium | Critical |
| 🟠 P1 | Testing (Vitest + Playwright) | Medium | High |
| 🟠 P1 | Lint/Type errors (61 issues) | Low | High |
| 🟠 P1 | Production deployment (Docker/VPS or Vercel Postgres) | Medium | High |
| 🟡 P2 | tRPC stable version | Low | Medium |
| 🟡 P2 | Paddle / Sentry / Qdrant | Medium | Medium |

Would you like me to create a detailed upgrade plan or start implementing any of these areas?

Now I have the full picture. The graph report powerfully validates and expands on the upgrade areas I identified. Let me break down the **most important upgrades** using both the code analysis and the graph topology:

---

## 1. Database Layer: The `#1 God Node` with 23 Edges

**Graph evidence:** `db` is the most connected node in the entire system. It bridges 5 major communities: *Database and API Setup*, *Agent-based Data Fetching*, *Logging and Event Bus*, *Scraper and Router Execution*, and *Pipeline Engine Core*.

**What this means:** `db` has **high betweenness centrality (0.036)** — it is a bottleneck. Any change to the database layer ripples through almost every subsystem. Right now it's raw SQLite with string-based SQL. This is your highest-risk, highest-impact upgrade.

**Action:** Migrate to PostgreSQL/MySQL + Drizzle ORM as documented. Because `db` is so central, use an abstraction layer (repository pattern) so the god node decouples from direct SQL strings.

---

## 2. The `run()` Script Coupling Problem

**Graph evidence:** The "Surprising Connections" section flags **inferred edges** where `run()` in `scripts/runOptimization.ts` and `scripts/testEndToEnd.ts` directly calls internal services (`buildCatalogGraph()`, `fetchCompetitors()`, `generateAllStageCopy()`).

**What this means:** Your CLI scripts are tightly coupled to internal service APIs. These are *inferred* (not explicitly imported) which suggests dynamic requires or brittle indirection. This breaks encapsulation.

**Action:** Scripts should call the **tRPC API** or a dedicated SDK, not reach into `api/services/` directly. Refactor scripts into a `scripts/lib/` layer that uses the public API surface.

---

## 3. 221 Isolated Nodes = Dead Code or Missing Implementation

**Graph evidence:** `STAGES`, `STAGE_NAMES`, `TaskStatus`, `QAPair`, `OptimizationReport`, and **216 others** have ≤1 connection.

**What this means:** Either:
- These are types/interfaces for features that were planned but never wired up
- They are dead code left from prototyping
- They are documentation artifacts without implementation

This maps directly to what I found: documented features (Paddle, Sentry, SP-API OAuth, Qdrant) with env vars but no real integration.

**Action:** Audit isolated nodes. Delete dead types. For "planned but not wired" nodes (likely the ~50 related to payments, auth, vector search), either implement or remove from the type surface to reduce maintenance burden.

---

## 4. "Agent-based Data Fetching" — Cohesion 0.09

**Graph evidence:** Community 0 has 35 nodes but almost no internal cohesion. The graph itself asks: *"Should this be split into smaller, more focused modules?"*

**What this means:** `ApifyFetcherAgent`, `CompetitorAnalystAgent`, `ListingFetcherAgent`, `OptimizationOrchestrator`, `PreprocessorAgent`, `STAGE_NAMES`, `STAGES` are all lumped together with weak interconnection. This community is a "junk drawer."

**Action:** Split into:
- `api/agents/fetchers/` (Apify, Listing, Scraper)
- `api/agents/analyzers/` (Competitor, Semantic)
- `api/pipeline/orchestrator/` (STAGES, STAGE_ORDER, engine)

---

## 5. "Database and API Setup" — Cohesion 0.06

**Graph evidence:** 47 nodes including `apiKeyProcedure`, `t`, `BookingRecord`, `db`, `dbDir`, `__dirname`, and 39 others — all in one low-cohesion blob.

**What this means:** Database schema, tRPC procedures, auth stubs, path utilities, and record types are all mixed together.

**Action:** Separate concerns:
- `api/db/schema.ts` → table definitions
- `api/db/types.ts` → record interfaces
- `api/trpc/` → tRPC setup, middleware, context
- `api/auth/` → authentication logic (currently missing)

---

## 6. Pipeline Engine: Actually Healthy

**Graph evidence:** *Pipeline Engine Core* has **cohesion 0.25** — the highest of any backend community. `PipelineEngine`, `STAGE_ORDER`, `StageExecutor`, and `StageContext` are tightly related.

**What this means:** This is one of the better-architected parts. Don't over-refactor this. The engine itself is fine — focus on what it calls (the agents in Community 0).

---

## Priority Matrix (Graph-Backed)

| Priority | Upgrade | Graph Signal | Why Now |
|----------|---------|------------|---------|
| **P0** | Database abstraction (`db` god node) | 23 edges, betweenness 0.036 | Central bottleneck; changes here affect 5 communities |
| **P0** | Auth system | `apiKeyProcedure` in low-cohesion DB community | Security; currently stubbed |
| **P1** | Refactor `run()` script coupling | 7 inferred edges to internal services | Breaks API boundaries; scripts should use public API |
| **P1** | Prune 221 isolated nodes | 37% of all nodes are orphans | Dead code confusion; likely unfinished features |
| **P1** | Split Agent community | Cohesion 0.09, 35 nodes | Improves maintainability, testability |
| **P2** | Decouple DB+API community | Cohesion 0.06, 47 nodes | Mixed concerns; hard to navigate |

---

Would you like me to:
1. **Create a migration plan** for the database layer (SQLite → PostgreSQL + Drizzle)?
2. **Refactor the scripts** to stop reaching into internal services?
3. **Audit and prune** the isolated nodes to find what's actually dead code vs. unfinished features?

Based on a pure reading of `graphify-out/GRAPH_REPORT.md`, here are the **most important areas to upgrade**, ranked by the graph's own structural signals:

---

## 1. The `db` God Node — Your #1 Architectural Bottleneck

**Graph signal:** `db` is the most connected node (23 edges) with the highest betweenness centrality (0.036). It bridges 5 distinct communities.

**What the graph is telling you:** Any change to the database layer affects *Agent-based Data Fetching*, *Logging/Event Bus*, *Scraper/Router Execution*, *HTTP Server Setup*, and *Pipeline Engine Core* simultaneously. The graph literally asks: *"Why does `db` connect all of these?"*

**Upgrade implication:** The database is a **monolithic coupling point**. If you're planning to migrate from SQLite (as the code confirms), this must be done with an abstraction layer first — otherwise you'll break 5 communities at once.

---

## 2. Two `run()` Functions with Inferred Cross-Boundary Calls

**Graph signal:** Two separate `run()` nodes (19 and 17 edges) have **7 and 6 inferred edges** respectively, connecting CLI scripts directly to internal services (`buildCatalogGraph()`, `fetchCompetitors()`, `generateAllStageCopy()`). The graph flags these as "surprising connections" and asks you to verify them.

**What the graph is telling you:** Scripts in `scripts/` are bypassing the API boundary and reaching into `api/services/`. These aren't explicit imports — the model had to infer them, suggesting dynamic or brittle coupling.

**Upgrade implication:** These scripts need to be decoupled. They should call the public API surface, not private service functions.

---

## 3. 221 Isolated Nodes = 37% of Your Codebase Is Disconnected

**Graph signal:** 221 nodes have ≤1 connection. Examples: `STAGES`, `STAGE_NAMES`, `TaskStatus`, `QAPair`, `OptimizationReport`. The graph explicitly calls this a "knowledge gap."

**What the graph is telling you:** More than a third of your symbols are orphans. They are either:
- **Dead code** (defined but never used)
- **Unfinished features** (types without implementation)
- **Documentation-only artifacts** (planned but not wired)

**Upgrade implication:** This is technical debt cleanup. These nodes clutter the graph, increase cognitive load, and suggest the gap between documentation and implementation is significant.

---

## 4. "Agent-based Data Fetching" — Lowest Cohesion Community (0.09)

**Graph signal:** 35 nodes lumped together with almost no internal interconnection. The graph itself asks: *"Should this be split into smaller, more focused modules?"*

**Nodes in this community:** `ApifyFetcherAgent`, `CompetitorAnalystAgent`, `ListingFetcherAgent`, `OptimizationOrchestrator`, `PreprocessorAgent`, `STAGE_NAMES`, `STAGES`, and 27 others.

**What the graph is telling you:** This is a "junk drawer" community. Fetchers, analyzers, orchestrators, and stage constants all share a community label but don't actually cohere.

**Upgrade implication:** Split into focused communities:
- `api/agents/fetchers/` (Apify, Listing)
- `api/agents/analyzers/` (Competitor, Semantic)
- `api/pipeline/orchestrator/` (OptimizationOrchestrator, STAGE_ORDER)

---

## 5. "Database and API Setup" — Second Lowest Cohesion (0.06)

**Graph signal:** 47 nodes including `apiKeyProcedure`, `t`, `BookingRecord`, `BrandSettingsRecord`, `CatalogLinkRecord`, `db`, `dbDir`, `__dirname`, and 39 others.

**What the graph is telling you:** Database schema, tRPC setup, auth stubs, path utilities, and record types are all mixed into one blob. There is no separation of concerns.

**Upgrade implication:** Refactor into distinct communities:
- `api/db/` — schema, migrations, client
- `api/trpc/` — router, context, middleware
- `api/auth/` — authentication (currently missing as a standalone community)

---

## 6. `PipelineState` — Another Cross-Community Bridge

**Graph signal:** Betweenness centrality 0.035. Connects *Agent-based Data Fetching* to *REPL and Logging*, *Admin Dashboard & Pipeline*, and *Pipeline Engine Core*.

**What the graph is telling you:** Pipeline state is bleeding across boundaries. The REPL/logging system, the admin UI, and the engine core all depend on the same state shape.

**Upgrade implication:** Define a strict `PipelineState` interface in a shared `types/` package and ensure each community only depends on the interface, not on concrete implementations from other communities.

---

## 7. Community 19 — "System Integration Architecture" Exists Only in Docs

**Graph signal:** This community has 10 nodes — `Amazon SP-API`, `ASIN Analysis Flow`, `Authentication Flow`, `Deployment Architecture`, `OpenAI API`, `Paddle Payments`, `Payment Flow`, `Sentry Integration` — but **zero code connections** to the rest of the graph. It only connects to the *Technical Architecture Document* node.

**What the graph is telling you:** These are documented integrations that are structurally isolated from the actual codebase. The graph sees them as words in a document, not as implemented systems.

**Upgrade implication:** These are the biggest "documentation vs. reality" gaps. Either implement them (connect them to the code graph) or remove them from the architecture docs.

---

## Priority Ranking (Graph-Only)

| Rank | Area | Graph Evidence | Action |
|:---:|---|---|---|
| **1** | `db` abstraction | God node #1, betweenness 0.036, bridges 5 communities | Add repository pattern before any DB migration |
| **2** | Script decoupling | 13 inferred edges from `run()` to internal services | Make scripts use public API only |
| **3** | Prune 221 orphans | 37% of nodes are isolated | Audit for dead code; finish or delete unfinished features |

| **6** | PipelineState boundary | Betweenness 0.035 | Extract strict interface, reduce cross-community deps |
| **7** | Documented-but-unimplemented systems | Community 19 has no code edges | Implement auth, payments, monitoring, SP-API or remove from docs |

---

**Bottom line from the graph:** Your architecture has clean separation in some places (*Pipeline Engine Core* has 0.25 cohesion — healthy) but suffers from **monolithic database coupling**, **script-to-service boundary violations**, and **a massive dead code surface**. Now I have the raw graph data analyzed. Let me synthesize the most important findings from this raw data analysis:

1. **154 cross-community links (14.3%)** - significant coupling between modules
2. **Top cross-community bridges:**
   - ProspectLanding.tsx (17/27 links cross-community) - this page touches everything

   - engine.ts (14/22) - pipeline engine has lots of external connections

   - 9 routers directly

   - boot.ts

   - Many communities are completely isolated (config, docs, images) - that's expected
   - Pipeline Engine Core has 30 internal / 30 external links - ratio of 1.0 means it's as connected outside as inside

Let me present this clearly to the user.

</details>

Based on the raw graph data (`graph.json`), here are the structural upgrade priorities revealed by the topology itself:

---

## 1. The `db` Instance: Imported by 23 Files Across 6 Communities

**Raw data:** The `db` node (`api/db/client.ts:49`) has **23 edges**. Every single one is an `imports` relation. It is directly imported by:

- **9 routers** (`agents.ts`, `analysis.ts`, `apollo.ts`, `booking.ts`, `branding.ts`, `catalogGraphRouter.ts`, `prospects.ts`, `rufusTracker.ts`, `scraper.ts`)
- **Pipeline engine + stages** (`engine.ts`, `stages.ts`)
- **Infrastructure** (`queue.ts`, `boot.ts`)
- **3 scripts** (`createGoPureProspect.ts`, `createMockProspect.ts`, `removeMockProspect.ts`)
- **2 scratch files** (`check_db.ts`, `test_db.ts`)

**Graph signal:** `db` is a **cross-community bridge** with 9 of its 23 connections reaching outside Community 1.

**What to upgrade:** There is **zero abstraction layer**. Every module talks directly to SQLite. Before any database migration, you must insert a repository/service boundary so that `db` stops being a god node.

---

## 2. `client.ts` File Is the Real God Node (Degree 39)

**Raw data:** The file node `client.ts` has **39 edges** — higher than the `db` instance itself (23). This is because `client.ts` exports both the `db` instance **and** all the TypeScript interfaces (`ProspectRecord`, `ListingRecord`, `BookingRecord`, etc.).

**What to upgrade:** Separate types from the database client. `client.ts` is doing double duty as a connection factory and a type definition file. Split into:
- `api/db/client.ts` — database connection only
- `api/db/types.ts` — record interfaces

This alone would drop `client.ts` from degree 39 to roughly degree 20.

---

## 3. `stages.ts` Bleeds Into 16 External Connections

**Raw data:** `api/pipeline/stages.ts` has 34 total edges, but **16 of them are cross-community** (47%). It is the #2 cross-community bridge after `ProspectLanding.tsx`.

**What to upgrade:** `stages.ts` likely imports executors from the agent community (Community 0) while living in the pipeline community (Community 12). The stage definitions should be pure data/config, while the executor imports should happen in `engine.ts` or a dedicated `executorMap.ts`. Decouple **stage order** from **stage implementation**.

---

## 4. `ProspectLanding.tsx`: 63% of Its Connections Are External

**Raw data:** `src/pages/ProspectLanding.tsx` has 27 total edges, **17 cross-community**. It imports from the landing components community, the prospect data community, the tRPC context community, and likely the router community.

**What to upgrade:** This page is acting as a **monolithic composition root** for the entire landing experience. It should be split into:
- `ProspectLanding.tsx` — routing/layout only
- `LandingPageSections.tsx` — section composition
- Individual sections already exist, but the page file is still doing too much orchestration.

---

## 5. 290 Orphaned Nodes (48.8% of the Graph)

**Raw data:** 290 nodes have degree ≤ 1. Breakdown:
- **245 code nodes** orphaned
- **Top orphan sources:** `package.json` (43), `tsconfig.*.json` (49 total), `docs/technical-architecture.md` (10), `api/db/client.ts` (9), `ErrorBoundary.tsx` (6)

**What to upgrade:** Nearly half your graph is dead weight. The `package.json` and `tsconfig` orphans are expected (dependency names, config keys), but **245 orphaned code nodes** means interfaces, functions, and types that are defined but never connected to anything else. This maps to the "documented but unimplemented" problem.

---

## 6. Pipeline Engine Core: 50% External Coupling

**Raw data:** Community 12 (*Pipeline Engine Core*) has 30 internal links and **30 external links** — ratio 1.00. It is as connected to the outside as it is to itself.

**What to upgrade:** Despite having the highest *reported* cohesion (0.25), the raw link data shows the engine is **heavily entangled** with other communities. The `engine.ts` file alone has 14 cross-community edges. The engine should not know about router-level concerns or agent implementations.

---

## 7. 154 Cross-Community Links (14.3% of All Edges)

**Raw data:** Out of 1,074 total links, 154 cross community boundaries.

**Top bridge nodes** (most cross-community links):
| Node | Cross-Community | Total | % External |
|---|---|---|---|
| `ProspectLanding.tsx` | 17 | 27 | 63% |
| `stages.ts` | 16 | 34 | 47% |
| `engine.ts` | 14 | 22 | 64% |
| `client.ts` | 11 | 39 | 28% |
| `db` | 9 | 23 | 39% |
| `types.ts` (pipeline) | 9 | 16 | 56% |
| `boot.ts` | 8 | 17 | 47% |
| `router.ts` | 8 | 21 | 38% |

---

## Summary: Graph-Backed Upgrade Priority

| Priority | Target | Graph Metric | Action |
|:---:|---|---|---|
| **P0** | `db` / `client.ts` | 39 edges, imported by 23 files, 9 cross-community | Extract repository layer; split types from client |
| **P0** | `stages.ts` | 16/34 edges cross-community | Decouple stage config from executor imports |
| **P1** | `ProspectLanding.tsx` | 17/27 edges cross-community | Split composition root into smaller coordinators |
| **P1** | `engine.ts` | 14/22 edges cross-community | Ensure engine only depends on stage interfaces, not concrete agents |
| **P2** | 245 orphaned code nodes | 48.8% of graph | Audit and delete dead code; implement documented features |

Would you like me to start implementing the `db` abstraction layer, or would you prefer to tackle the `stages.ts` decoupling first?

```json
{
  "command": "node -e \"\nconst fs = require('fs');\nconst data = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('graphify-out/graph.json', 'utf8'));\n\n// Find potential import cycles at file level\nconst fileImports = {};\ndata.links.forEach(l => {\n  if (l.relation === 'imports' || l.relation === 'imports_from') {\n    const s = data.nodes.find(n => n.id === l.source);\n    const t = data.nodes.find(n => n.id === l.target);\n    if (s && t && s.source_file && t.source_file && s.source_file !== t.source_file) {\n      const from = s.source_file;\n      const to = t.source_file;\n      if (!fileImports[from]) fileImports[from] = new Set();\n      fileImports[from].add(to);\n    }\n  }\n});\n\n// Detect cycles (length 2 and 3)\nconst cycles = [];\nObject.keys(fileImports).forEach(a => {\n  fileImports[a].forEach(b => {\n    if (fileImports[b] && fileImports[b].has(a)) {\n      if (a < b) cycles.push([a, b]); // dedup\n    }\n    // length 3\n    if (fileImports[b]) {\n      fileImports[b].forEach(c => {\n        if (c !== a && fileImports[c] && fileImports[c].has(a)) {\n          const key = [a,b,c].sort().join('|');\n          if (!cycles.find(x => x.join('|') === key)) {\n            cycles.push([a,b,c]);\n          }\n        }\n      });\n    }\n  });\n});\n\nconsole.log('=== IMPORT CYCLES ===');\nconsole.log('2-way cycles:', cycles.filter(c => c.length === 2).length);\ncycles.filter(c => c.length === 2).slice(0, 5).forEach(c => console.log(' ', c.join(' <-> ')));\nconsole.log('3-way cycles:', cycles.filter(c => c.length === 3).length);\ncycles.filter(c => c.length === 3).slice(0, 5).forEach(c => console.log(' ', c.join(' -> ')));\n\""
}
```

Based on the raw `graph.json` data (594 nodes, 1074 links, 154 cross-community edges), here is the definitive structural analysis:

---

## 1. The `db` God Node: 23 Direct Consumers, 9 Cross-Community

**Raw fact:** The `db` instance is imported by **23 separate files** across 6 communities.

**Exact import graph of `db`:**
```
db -> apifyFetcher.ts (comm 0)
db -> boot.ts (comm 5)
db -> schema.ts (comm 1)
db -> queue.ts (comm 2)
db -> runner.ts (comm 1)
db -> engine.ts (comm 12)
db -> stages.ts (comm 0)
db -> agents.ts (comm 1)
db -> analysis.ts (comm 1)
db -> apollo.ts (comm 1)
db -> booking.ts (comm 1)
db -> branding.ts (comm 1)
db -> catalogGraphRouter.ts (comm 4)
db -> prospects.ts (comm 1)
db -> rufusTracker.ts (comm 4)
db -> scraper.ts (comm 4)
db -> check_db.ts (comm 1)
db -> test_db.ts (comm 1)
db -> createGoPureProspect.ts (comm 1)
db -> createMockProspect.ts (comm 1)
db -> removeMockProspect.ts (comm 1)
db -> tokenBudget.ts (comm 2)
```

**Structural problem:** Every router, the pipeline engine, the queue, and even scratch scripts talk directly to SQLite. There is no repository boundary.

---

## 2. `client.ts` Is the Real Bottleneck (Degree 39)

**Raw fact:** `api/db/client.ts` is the highest-degree node in the entire graph (39 edges). It beats `db` itself because it exports both the connection **and** 15 TypeScript interfaces.

**Nodes inside `client.ts` with their degrees:**
| Node | Degree | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `client.ts` (file) | 39 | Barrel + connection factory |
| `db` | 23 | SQLite instance |
| `ProspectRecord` | 4 | Type interface |
| `ListingRecord` | 4 | Type interface |
| `ListingAnalysisRecord` | 2 | Type interface |
| `BookingRecord` | 2 | Type interface |
| `BrandSettingsRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `RufusQueryRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `CatalogLinkRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `PipelineJobRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `PipelineJobStageRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `UsageEventRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `JobQueueRecord` | 1 | Type interface |
| `withTransaction()` | 2 | Helper function |
| `__dirname` | 1 | Path var |
| `dbDir` | 1 | Path var |

**Structural problem:** One file is doing connection management, type definitions, and utility functions. Splitting types into a separate file would immediately drop its degree from 39 to ~24.

---

## 3. Community 1 ("Database and API Setup") Is a Junk Drawer

**Raw fact:** 69 nodes, 131 internal links, 60 external links. But look at what's *inside* it:

- **Database files:** `client.ts`, `schema.ts`, `runner.ts`, `check_db.ts`, `test_db.ts`
- **Routers:** `agents.ts`, `analysis.ts`, `apollo.ts`, `booking.ts`, `branding.ts`, `prospects.ts`
- **Services:** `apollo.ts` (service), `copywriter.ts`, `webhook.ts`
- **Scripts:** `createGoPureProspect.ts`, `createMockProspect.ts`, `removeMockProspect.ts`
- **Infra:** `trpc.ts`

**Structural problem:** This community mixes database schema, API routers, external services, and CLI scripts. It has the second-highest external coupling in the entire graph (60 cross-community links).

---

## 4. `stages.ts` and `engine.ts` Are Pipeline Leaks

**Raw fact:** `stages.ts` has 34 edges, **16 cross-community** (47%). `engine.ts` has 22 edges, **14 cross-community** (64%).

**The leak:** `stages.ts` is in Community 0 (*Agent-based Data Fetching*) but it imports from the pipeline core (Community 12). `engine.ts` is in Community 12 (*Pipeline Engine Core*) but imports from Community 0. They form a **two-way bridge** between communities.

**Structural problem:** Stage definitions and stage executors are co-located in `stages.ts`, forcing the pipeline engine to reach into the agent community to run stages.

---

## 5. 290 Orphaned Nodes = 48.8% of the Graph

**Raw fact:** Nearly half the nodes have degree ≤ 1.

**Breakdown by type:**
- **245 code nodes** orphaned
- **19 document nodes** orphaned  
- **15 image nodes** orphaned
- **11 concept nodes** orphaned

**Top files producing orphans:**
| File | Orphans | Cause |
|---|---|---|
| `package.json` | 43 | Dependency names |
| `tsconfig.app.json` | 17 | Compiler options |
| `tsconfig.node.json` | 16 | Compiler options |
| `tsconfig.server.json` | 16 | Compiler options |
| `technical-architecture.md` | 10 | Document headings |
| `api/db/client.ts` | 9 | Record interfaces (unused) |
| `examples/sentry/README.md` | 7 | Documentation |
| `api/infra/queue.ts` | 6 | Internal methods |

**Structural problem:** 245 code orphans means interfaces, functions, and types that exist but are never referenced by anything else in the graph.

---

## 6. `ProspectLanding.tsx` Is a Frontend Monolith

**Raw fact:** `src/pages/ProspectLanding.tsx` imports from **8 distinct communities** — the most of any file in the graph.

**Cross-community links from ProspectLanding.tsx:** 17 of 27 total edges (63%).

**Structural problem:** This single page file is the primary integration point for the landing page, pulling in components, hooks, types, and data mapping from across the frontend graph.

---

## 7. Only 6 Cross-Community `calls` Relations

**Raw fact:** Out of 95 total `calls` edges, only 6 cross community boundaries:

| Caller | Callee | Violation |
|---|---|---|
| `competitorAnalyst.ts` → `fetchCompetitors()` | `api/services/competitor.ts` | Agent calls service directly |
| `listingFetcher.ts` → `scrapeAmazonListing()` | `api/services/scraper.ts` | Agent calls service directly |
| `scripts/testEndToEnd.ts` → `generateAllStageCopy()` | `api/services/copywriter.ts` | Script bypasses API |
| `api/services/optimization.ts` → `log()` | `scripts/repl.ts` | Service calls REPL script (!) |
| `scripts/runOptimization.ts` → `generatePackageCopy()` | itself | Self-call |
| `ProspectLanding.tsx` → `useActivityTracker` | `src/hooks/useActivityTracker.ts` | Normal hook usage |

**Critical finding:** `api/services/optimization.ts` calls `log()` in `scripts/repl.ts`. A core service is calling into a CLI script. This is a backwards dependency.

---

## 8. `api/pipeline/types.ts` Is Misplaced

**Raw fact:** `types.ts` (pipeline) is assigned to Community 12 (*Pipeline Engine Core*) but has **9 links to Community 0** and only **7 links within Community 12**.

**Structural problem:** The pipeline types are more connected to the agent community than to the pipeline community. The types likely reference agent-specific shapes, causing the pipeline to leak into agent concerns.

---

## 9. No Import Cycles (Good News)

**Raw fact:** Zero 2-way and zero 3-way cycles detected at the file level.

**Structural health:** The graph is a DAG at the file level. This means refactoring can proceed safely without circular dependency nightmares.

---

## Upgrade Priority (Graph-Quantified)

| Priority | Target | Metric | Action |
|:---:|---|---|---|
| **P0** | `client.ts` / `db` | Degree 39, 23 imports, 9 cross-community | Extract repository layer; split types to `api/db/types.ts` |
| **P0** | Community 1 | 69 nodes, 60 external links, cohesion 0.06 | Split into `db/`, `routers/`, `services/`, `scripts/` communities |
| **P1** | `stages.ts` ↔ `engine.ts` | 30 cross-community links combined | Decouple stage config from executors |
| **P1** | `ProspectLanding.tsx` | Imports from 8 communities | Split into layout + section composition |
| **P1** | `api/services/optimization.ts` | Calls `scripts/repl.ts` | Remove backwards dependency; use `api/infra/logger.ts` |
| **P2** | 245 code orphans | 48.8% of graph | Audit for dead code vs. unfinished features |
| **P2** | `api/pipeline/types.ts` | More links to comm 0 than comm 12 | Move to shared types or decouple from agent shapes |

The graph data makes one thing unambiguous: **Community 1 and the `db` node are your architectural chokepoints.** Every other problem either stems from them or is secondary to them.

     8	// Allow custom DB path via environment variable (essential for VPS deployments to persist data outside the code directory)
     9	const bundledDbPath = process.env.DB_PATH
    10	  ? path.resolve(process.env.DB_PATH)
    11	  : path.resolve(__dirname, "../../data/optimus.db");
    12	
    13	const isVercel = !!process.env.VERCEL;
    14	
    15	/**
    16	 * On Vercel, the bundled DB file is inside the read-only deployment bundle.
    17	 * We copy it to /tmp (the only writable directory in a serverless function)
    18	 * so that mutation endpoints (bookings, views, activities) can write.
    19	 * 
    20	 * ⚠️ CRITICAL: /tmp is ephemeral — data does not persist across cold starts.
    21	 * All writes (prospects, bookings, activities, pipeline jobs) are LOST when
    22	 * the function instance recycles. For production persistence, migrate to:
    23	 *   - PostgreSQL (Neon, Supabase, Railway)
    24	 *   - MySQL (PlanetScale, RDS)
    25	 *   - Or use Vercel Postgres / Vercel Blob for specific data
    26	 * 
    27	 * This SQLite setup is suitable for demos and local development only.
    28	 */
    29	let dbPath: string;
    30	
    31	if (isVercel) {
    32	  const tmpDbPath = "/tmp/optimus.db";
    33	  if (!fs.existsSync(tmpDbPath) && fs.existsSync(bundledDbPath)) {
    34	    fs.copyFileSync(bundledDbPath, tmpDbPath);
    35	    console.log(`📋 Copied bundled DB to writable /tmp for Vercel.`);
    36	  }

    38	} else {

   255	/**
   256	 * Execute a function within an explicit SQLite transaction.
   257	 * Automatically commits on success, rolls back on error.
   258	 */
   259	export function withTransaction<T>(fn: (db: Database.Database) => T): T {
   260	  db.prepare("BEGIN").run();
   261	  try {
   262	    const result = fn(db);
   263	    db.prepare("COMMIT").run();
   264	    return result;
   265	  } catch (err) {
   266	    db.prepare("ROLLBACK").run();
   267	    throw err;
   268	  }
   269	}
   270	
   271	export async function withTransactionAsync<T>(
   272	  fn: (db: Database.Database) => Promise<T>
   273	): Promise<T> {
   274	  db.prepare("BEGIN").run();
   275	  try {
   276	    const result = await fn(db);
   277	    db.prepare("COMMIT").run();
   278	    return result;
   279	  } catch (err) {
   280	    db.prepare("ROLLBACK").run();
   281	    throw err;
   282	  }
   283	}

    18	const reviewer = new ReviewerAgent();
    19	
    20	async function runReviewer(
    21	  stageName: StageName,
    22	  output: StageOutput[keyof StageOutput]
    23	): Promise<{ approved: boolean; issues: string[]; score: number }> {
    24	  const task: AgentTask = {
    25	    id: `review-${stageName}-${Date.now()}`,
    26	    asin: "",
    27	    marketplace: "US",
    28	    role: stageName === "fetch" ? "apify_fetcher" :
    29	          stageName === "preprocess" ? "preprocessor" :
    30	          stageName === "embedding" ? "embedding_generator" :
    31	          stageName === "semantic" ? "semantic_analyzer" :
    32	          stageName === "optimize" ? "content_optimizer" :
    33	          stageName === "competitor" ? "competitor_analyst" : "apify_fetcher",
    34	    status: "completed",
    35	    input: null,
    36	    output,
    37	    attempt: 1,
    38	    maxAttempts: 3,
    39	  };
    40	
    41	  const review = await reviewer.review(task);
    42	  if (!review.approved && review.issues.length > 0) {
    43	    eventBus.emit("review:warning", {
    44	      stage: stageName,
    45	      issues: review.issues,
    46	      score: review.score,
    47	    });
    48	  }
    49	  return { approved: review.approved, issues: review.issues, score: review.score };
    50	}

    52	export const stageExecutors: StageExecutor[] = [

    56	    async execute(ctx: StageContext) {

    58	      eventBus.emit("stage:start", { jobId: ctx.jobId, stage: "fetch" }, ctx.correlationId);

    70

    14	export const app = new Hono();

    16	// A simple serveStatic replacement using Node fs for portable and error-free execution
    17	function serveStatic(options: { root?: string; path?: string }) {
    18	  return async (c: Context, next: () => Promise<void>) => {
    19	    let filePath = options.path;
    20	    if (!filePath && options.root) {
    21	      const urlPath = c.req.path;
    22	      filePath = path.join(options.root, urlPath);
    23	    }
    24	    
    25	    if (filePath && fs.existsSync(filePath) && fs.statSync(filePath).isFile()) {
    26	      const content = fs.readFileSync(filePath);
    27	      const ext = path.extname(filePath).toLowerCase();
    28	      const mimeTypes: Record<string, string> = {
    29	        ".html": "text/html",
    30	        ".css": "text/css",
    31	        ".js": "application/javascript",
    32	        ".json": "application/json",
    33	        ".png": "image/png",
    34	        ".jpg": "image/jpeg",
    35	        ".gif": "image/gif",
    36	        ".svg": "image/svg+xml",
    37	        ".ico": "image/x-icon",
    38	      };
    39	      c.header("Content-Type", mimeTypes[ext] || "application/octet-stream");
    40	      return c.body(content);
    41	    }
    42	    await next();
    43	  };
    44	}
    45	
    46	// CORS — restrict in production, allow all in development
    47	const allowedOrigins = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGINS
    48	  ? process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGINS.split(",").map((o) => o.trim())
    49	  : process.env.NODE_ENV === "production"
    50	    ? []
    51	    : ["*"];
    52	
    53	app.use("*", cors({
    54	  origin: (origin) => {
    55	    if (!origin) return origin;
    56	    if (allowedOrigins.includes("*")) return origin;
    57	    if (allowedOrigins.includes(origin)) return origin;
    58	    return null;
    59	  },
    60	}));
    61

    85	    return c.text(`Failed to generate PDF: ${err.message}`, 500);
    86	  }

   109	
   110	// Bun/Deno/Node compatibility
   111	
   112	// Node native fetch server
   113	import { createServer } from "http";
   114	
   115	const httpServer = createServer(async (req, res) => {
   116	  const url = new URL(req.url || "/", `http://${req.headers.host}`);
   117	  const request = new Request(url, {
   118	    method: req.method,
   119	    headers: new Headers(
   120	      Object.entries(req.headers).map(([k, v]) => [k, Array.isArray(v) ? v.join(", ") : v || ""]) as any
   121	    ),
   122	    // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
   123	    body: (req.method !== "GET" && req.method !== "HEAD" ? await getBody(req) : undefined) as any,
   124	  });
   125	
   126	  const response = await app.fetch(request);
   127	
   128	  res.statusCode = response.status;
   129	  response.headers.forEach((value, key) => {
   130	    res.setHeader(key, value);
   131	  });
   132	
   133	  if (response.body) {
   134	    const reader = response.body.getReader();
   135	    while (true) {
   136	      const { done, value } = await reader.read();
   137	      if (done) break;
   138	      res.write(Buffer.from(value));
   139	    }
   140	  }
   141	  res.end();
   142	});
   143	
   144	function getBody(req: import("http").IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {
   145	  return new Promise((resolve) => {
   146	    const chunks: Buffer[] = [];
   147	    req.on("data", (chunk) => chunks.push(chunk));
   148	    req.on("end", () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)));
   149	  });
   150	}
   151	
   152	if (!process.env.VERCEL) {
   153	  httpServer.listen(port, () => {
   154	    console.log(`🚀 Server listening on http://localhost:${port}`);
   155	    console.log(`📡 tRPC endpoint: http://localhost:${port}/api/trpc`);
   156	    console.log(`📊 SSE endpoint: http://localhost:${port}/api/sse/pipeline/:jobId`);
   157	
   158	    // Start background job worker for non-serverless environments
   159	    queueWorker.start();
   160	  });
   161	}
