     7	function generateSlug(): string {
     8	  return Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 10);
     9	}
    10	
    11	export const prospectsRouter = router({
    12	  create: publicProcedure
    13	    .input(
    14	      z.object({
    15	        email: z.string().email(),
    16	        firstName: z.string().optional(),
    17	        lastName: z.string().optional(),
    18	        company: z.string().optional(),
    19	        asin: z.string().optional(),
    20	        marketplace: z.string().optional(),
    21	        packageType: z.string().optional(),
    22	        pricePoint: z.number().optional(),
    23	      })
    24	    )
    25	    .mutation(async ({ input }) => {
    26	      const slug = generateSlug();
    27	      const result = db
    28	        .prepare(
    29	          `INSERT INTO prospects (slug, email, firstName, lastName, company, status, landingPageViews, packageType, pricePoint, createdAt)
    30	         VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, 'new', 0, ?, ?, datetime('now'))`
    31	        )
    32	        .run(
    33	          slug,
    34	          input.email,
    35	          input.firstName || null,
    36	          input.lastName || null,
    37	          input.company || null,
    38	          input.packageType || 'package_2',
    39	          input.pricePoint ?? 1500
    40	        );
    41	
    42	      return db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE id = ?").get(result.lastInsertRowid) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
    43	    }),
    44	
    45	  getBySlug: publicProcedure
    46	    .input(z.object({ slug: z.string() }))
    47	    .query(async ({ input }) => {
    48	      const prospect = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE slug = ?").get(input.slug) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
    49	      if (!prospect) {
    50	        throw new Error(`Prospect not found: ${input.slug}`);
    51	      }
    52	
    53	      const listing = db
    54	        .prepare("SELECT * FROM listings WHERE prospectId = ? ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1")
    55	        .get(prospect.id) as ListingRecord | undefined;
    56	      const analysis = listing
    57	        ? (db
    58	            .prepare("SELECT * FROM listing_analyses WHERE listingId = ? ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1")
    59	            .get(listing.id) as ListingAnalysisRecord | undefined)
    60	        : null;
    61	
    62	      return { prospect, listing: listing || null, analysis: analysis || null };
    63	    }),
    64	
    65	  list: publicProcedure
    66	    .input(
    67	      z.object({
    68	        status: z.string().optional(),
    69	        limit: z.number().int().min(1).max(100).optional().default(50),
    70	        offset: z.number().int().min(0).optional().default(0),
    71	      })
    72	    )
    73	    .query(({ input }) => {
    74	      let whereClause = "";
    75	      const params: (string | number)[] = [];
    76	      if (input.status) {
    77	        whereClause = "WHERE p.status = ?";
    78	        params.push(input.status);
    79	      }
    80	
    81	      const countRow = db
    82	        .prepare(`SELECT COUNT(*) as count FROM prospects p ${whereClause}`)
    83	        .get(...params) as { count: number };
    84	      const rows = db
    85	        .prepare(
    86	          `SELECT p.*, l.asin
    87	           FROM prospects p
    88	           LEFT JOIN listings l ON l.prospectId = p.id
    89	           AND l.id = (SELECT id FROM listings WHERE prospectId = p.id ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1)
    90	           ${whereClause}
    91	           ORDER BY p.createdAt DESC
    92	           LIMIT ? OFFSET ?`
    93	        )
    94	        .all(...params, input.limit, input.offset);
    95	
    96	      return { items: rows, count: countRow.count };
    97	    }),
    98	
    99	  getById: publicProcedure
   100	    .input(z.object({ id: z.number().int() }))
   101	    .query(({ input }) => {
   102	      const prospect = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE id = ?").get(input.id) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
   103	      if (!prospect) {
   104	        throw new Error(`Prospect not found: ${input.id}`);
   105	      }
   106	
   107	      const listing = db
   108	        .prepare("SELECT * FROM listings WHERE prospectId = ? ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1")
   109	        .get(prospect.id) as ListingRecord | undefined;
   110	      const analysis = listing
   111	        ? (db
   112	            .prepare("SELECT * FROM listing_analyses WHERE listingId = ? ORDER BY createdAt DESC LIMIT 1")
   113	            .get(listing.id) as ListingAnalysisRecord | undefined)
   114	        : null;
   115	      const bookings = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM bookings WHERE prospectId = ? ORDER BY createdAt DESC").all(prospect.id);
   116	
   117	      return { prospect, listing: listing || null, analysis: analysis || null, bookings: bookings || [] };
   118	    }),
   119	
   120	  updateStatus: publicProcedure
   121	    .input(z.object({ id: z.number().int(), status: z.string() }))
   122	    .mutation(({ input }) => {
   123	      db.prepare("UPDATE prospects SET status = ? WHERE id = ?").run(input.status, input.id);
   124	      return db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE id = ?").get(input.id) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
   125	    }),
   126	
   127	  incrementViews: publicProcedure
   128	    .input(z.object({ slug: z.string() }))
   129	    .mutation(({ input }) => {
   130	      db.prepare("UPDATE prospects SET landingPageViews = landingPageViews + 1 WHERE slug = ?").run(input.slug);
   131	      return db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE slug = ?").get(input.slug) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
   132	    }),
   133	
   134	  recordActivity: publicProcedure
   135	    .input(
   136	      z.object({
   137	        prospectId: z.number().int(),
   138	        eventType: z.string(),
   139	        eventData: z.record(z.any()).optional(),
   140	        interestScore: z.number().optional().default(0),
   141	      })
   142	    )
   143	    .mutation(async ({ input }) => {
   144	      // 1. Log event to database
   145	      try {
   146	        db.prepare(
   147	          `INSERT INTO prospect_activities (prospectId, eventType, eventData)
   148	           VALUES (?, ?, ?)`
   149	        ).run(input.prospectId, input.eventType, JSON.stringify(input.eventData || null));
   150	      } catch (err) {
   151	        console.error("❌ Failed to write activity to SQLite:", err);
   152	      }
   153	
   154	      // 2. Fetch prospect details to populate webhook notifications
   155	      let prospectInfo = { name: "Unknown Prospect", company: undefined as string | undefined, email: undefined as string | undefined };
   156	      try {
   157	        const prospect = db.prepare("SELECT firstName, lastName, company, email FROM prospects WHERE id = ?").get(input.prospectId) as {
   158	          firstName?: string;
   159	          lastName?: string;
   160	          company?: string;
   161	          email?: string;
   162	        } | undefined;
   163	
   164	        if (prospect) {
   165	          const name = [prospect.firstName, prospect.lastName].filter(Boolean).join(" ") || prospect.email || "Unknown Prospect";
   166	          prospectInfo = { name, company: prospect.company, email: prospect.email };
   167	        }
   168	      } catch (err) {
   169	        console.error("⚠️ Failed to read prospect details for webhook, using fallback:", err);
   170	      }
   171	
   172	      // Trigger webhook notification
   173	      await triggerWebhook(
   174	        prospectInfo,
   175	        input.eventType,
   176	        input.eventData,
   177	        input.interestScore
   178	      );
   179	
   180	      return { success: true };
   181	    }),
   182	});

     1	import { z } from "zod";
     2	import { db } from "../db/client.js";

     9	function safeJsonParse<T>(str: string | null | undefined, fallback: T): T {
    10	  if (!str) return fallback;
    11	  try {
    12	    return JSON.parse(str) as T;
    13	  } catch {
    14	    return fallback;
    15	  }
    16	}
    17	
    18	async function runAnalysis(listingId: number) {
    19	  const listing = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM listings WHERE id = ?").get(listingId) as ListingRecord | undefined;
    20	  if (!listing) {
    21	    throw new Error(`Listing not found: ${listingId}`);
    22	  }
    23	
    24	  const prospect = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects WHERE id = ?").get(listing.prospectId) as ProspectRecord | undefined;
    25	  if (!prospect) {
    26	    throw new Error(`Prospect not found for listing: ${listingId}`);
    27	  }
    28	
    29	  // Run the new resumable pipeline engine synchronously for backward compatibility
    30	  const job = await pipelineEngine.createAndRunJob(
    31	    listing.prospectId,
    32	    listing.id,
    33	    prospect.packageType || "package_2"
    34	  );
    35	
    36	  if (job.status === "failed") {
    37	    throw new Error(`Pipeline failed: ${job.errorLog || "Unknown error"}`);
    38	  }
    39	
    40	  // Extract stage outputs
    41	  const semanticStage = job.stages.semantic;
    42	  const optimizeStage = job.stages.optimize;
    43	  const competitorStage = job.stages.competitor;
    44	
    45	  const analysisResult = semanticStage?.output as AnalysisResult | undefined;
    46	  const optimized = optimizeStage?.output as
    47	    | ({ stageCopy?: unknown } & Record<string, unknown>)
    48	    | undefined;
    49	  const competitors = competitorStage?.output as Array<Record<string, unknown>> | undefined;
    50	
    51	  const rawListing: RawListingData = {
    52	    asin: listing.asin,
    53	    title: listing.title || "",
    54	    bullets: safeJsonParse(listing.bullets, []),
    55	    description: listing.description || "",
    56	    brand: listing.brand || "",
    57	    category: listing.category || "",
    58	    subcategory: listing.category || "",
    59	    images: safeJsonParse(listing.images, []),
    60	    price: listing.price || 0,
    61	    rating: listing.rating || 0,
    62	    reviewCount: listing.reviewCount || 0,
    63	    attributes: safeJsonParse(listing.rawScrapeData, {}),
    64	  };
    65	
    66	  const gaps = analysisResult?.semanticGaps || [];
    67	  const topIssues = gaps
    68	    .filter((g) => g.priority === "critical" || g.priority === "high")
    69	    .slice(0, 5);
    70	  const strengths = gaps.filter((g) => g.gap < 0.3).map((g) => g.dimension);
    71	  const opportunities = gaps.filter((g) => g.gap >= 0.3).map((g) => g.dimension);
    72	
    73	  const firstName = prospect.firstName || "";
    74	  const lastName = prospect.lastName || "";
    75	  const prospectName = [firstName, lastName].filter(Boolean).join(" ") || "there";
    76	
    77	  // Use stage copy from pipeline if available, otherwise generate fresh
    78	  let stageCopy = optimized?.stageCopy as
    79	    | {
    80	        heroHeadline: string;
    81	        heroSubheadline: string;
    82	        autopsyHeadline: string;
    83	        autopsyBody: string;
    84	        bleedHeadline: string;
    85	        bleedBody: string;
    86	        simulatorIntro: string;
    87	        simulatorScenarios: unknown;
    88	        transformHeadline: string;
    89	        transformBefore: unknown;
    90	        transformAfter: unknown;
    91	        roadmapHeadline: string;
    92	        roadmapBody: string;
    93	        socialProofHeadline: string;
    94	        urgencyCTA: string;
    95	        ctaHeadline: string;
    96	        ctaGuarantee: string;
    97	      }
    98	    | undefined;
    99	
   100	  if (!stageCopy) {
   101	    stageCopy = await generateAllStageCopy(
   102	      {
   103	        rufusScore: analysisResult?.rufusScore ?? 0,
   104	        cosmoScore: analysisResult?.cosmoScore ?? 0,
   105	        semanticGaps: gaps,
   106	      },
   107	      rawListing,
   108	      prospectName
   109	    );
   110	  }
   111	
   112	  const rufusScore = analysisResult?.rufusScore ?? 0;
   113	  // Calculate optimized score based on actual gap remediation potential
   114	  // rather than random inflation. If gaps were addressed, score improves
   115	  // proportionally to critical/high gap coverage.
   116	  const criticalGaps = gaps.filter((g) => g.priority === "critical" || g.priority === "high");
   117	  const gapRemediationPotential = criticalGaps.length > 0
   118	    ? Math.min(25, criticalGaps.length * 5)
   119	    : 10;
   120	  const optimizedRufusScore = Math.min(100, rufusScore + gapRemediationPotential);
   121	
   122	  const result = db.transaction(() => {
   123	    const insertResult = db
   124	      .prepare(
   125	        `INSERT INTO listing_analyses (
   126	          listingId, prospectId, overallScore, rufusScore, cosmoScore, semanticScore, contentScore, visualScore,
   127	          gaps, topIssues, strengths, opportunities, aiAnalysisRaw,
   128	          copyPersonalizedHook, copyProblemNarrative, copySolutionPitch, copyUrgencyCTA,
   129	          copyHeroHeadline, copyHeroSubheadline,
   130	          copyAutopsyHeadline, copyAutopsyBody,
   131	          copyBleedHeadline, copyBleedBody,
   132	          copySimulatorIntro, copySimulatorScenarios,
   133	          copyTransformHeadline, copyTransformBefore, copyTransformAfter,
   134	          copyRoadmapHeadline, copyRoadmapBody,
   135	          copySocialProofHeadline,
   136	          copyCtaHeadline, copyCtaGuarantee,
   137	          createdAt
   138	        ) VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, datetime('now'))`
   139	      )
   140	      .run(
   141	        listing.id,
   142	        listing.prospectId,
   143	        optimizedRufusScore,
   144	        rufusScore,
   145	        analysisResult?.cosmoScore || 0,
   146	        Math.round(rufusScore * 0.9),
   147	        Math.round(optimizedRufusScore * 0.95),
   148	        Math.round((analysisResult?.cosmoScore || 0) * 0.85),
   149	        JSON.stringify(gaps),
   150	        JSON.stringify(topIssues),
   151	        JSON.stringify(strengths),
   152	        JSON.stringify(opportunities),
   153	        JSON.stringify({ jobId: job.id, stages: Object.keys(job.stages) }),
   154	        stageCopy.heroHeadline,
   155	        stageCopy.autopsyBody,
   156	        stageCopy.roadmapBody,
   157	        stageCopy.urgencyCTA,
   158	        stageCopy.heroHeadline,
   159	        stageCopy.heroSubheadline,
   160	        stageCopy.autopsyHeadline,
   161	        stageCopy.autopsyBody,
   162	        stageCopy.bleedHeadline,
   163	        stageCopy.bleedBody,
   164	        stageCopy.simulatorIntro,
   165	        JSON.stringify(stageCopy.simulatorScenarios),
   166	        stageCopy.transformHeadline,
   167	        JSON.stringify(stageCopy.transformBefore),
   168	        JSON.stringify(stageCopy.transformAfter),
   169	        stageCopy.roadmapHeadline,
   170	        stageCopy.roadmapBody,
   171	        stageCopy.socialProofHeadline,
   172	        stageCopy.ctaHeadline,
   173	        stageCopy.ctaGuarantee
   174	      );
   175	
   176	    db.prepare("UPDATE prospects SET status = 'analyzed' WHERE id = ?").run(listing.prospectId);
   177	    return insertResult;
   178	  })();
   179	
   180	  const analysisRow = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM listing_analyses WHERE id = ?").get(result.lastInsertRowid);
   181	  return { analysis: analysisRow, listing, prospect };
   182	}

   184	export const analysisRouter = router({

     1	import type { OptimizedContent, SemanticGap, RawListingData } from "../agents/types.js";

     3	/**
     4	 * Stub: Generate optimized title, bullets, and Q&A.
     5	 */
     6	export async function generateOptimizedContent(
     7	  gaps: SemanticGap[],
     8	  listing: RawListingData
     9	): Promise<OptimizedContent> {
    10	  await delay(400 + Math.random() * 400);
    11	
    12	  const topGaps = gaps.slice(0, 3).map((g) => g.dimension.replace(/_/g, " "));
    13	  const brand = listing.brand || "Premium Brand";
    14	  const category = listing.category || "Health Product";
    15	  const existingTitle = listing.title || `${brand} ${category}`;
    16	
    17	  const title = `${brand} ${category} — ${topGaps.join(", ")} | ${existingTitle.split("|")[0]?.trim() || "Premium Quality"}, Third-Party Tested`;
    18	
    19	  const bullets = [
    20	    `Clinically Studied Formulation: Our ${category.toLowerCase()} delivers superior bioavailability — gentle on your system and optimized for maximum absorption.`,
    21	    `Supports ${topGaps[0] || "Core Benefits"}: Specifically formulated to address your primary needs. Backed by research and trusted by thousands of satisfied customers.`,
    22	    `${topGaps[1] || "Advanced Quality"} for Every Lifestyle: Perfect for health-conscious consumers looking for reliable, effective ${category.toLowerCase()} solutions.`,
    23	    `Third-Party Tested & Certified: Manufactured in a GMP-certified facility. Every batch is independently verified for purity, potency, and safety.`,

    43	      category: "safety",
    44	      priority: "high" as const,
    45	    },

    48	      optimizedAnswer: `Most customers report noticeable benefits within 1-2 weeks of consistent daily use. Individual results may vary based on lifestyle and usage consistency.`,
    49	      category: "usage",
    50	      priority: "medium" as const,
    51	    },
    52	    {

    54	      optimizedAnswer: `Yes, our ${category.toLowerCase()} is designed to complement a balanced routine. For best results, follow the recommended dosage and consult your healthcare provider if combining with other supplements.`,
    55	      category: "usage",
    56	      priority: "medium" as const,
    57	    },
    58	  ];
    59	
    60	  return {
    61	    title: title.slice(0, 200),
    62	    bullets,
    63	    description: `<p>${title}</p><ul>${bullets.map((b) => `<li>${b}</li>`).join("")}</ul>`,
    64	    qas,
    65	  };
    66	}

    68	function delay(ms: number): Promise<void> {
    69	  return new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));

    25	function isValidCssColor(color: string): boolean {
    26	  // Strict validation: only hex colors (#rgb or #rrggbb) or known safe keywords
    27	  const safeKeywords = ['transparent', 'inherit', 'initial', 'unset'];
    28	  if (safeKeywords.includes(color.toLowerCase())) return true;
    29	  return /^#([0-9A-Fa-f]{3}){1,2}$/.test(color);
    30	}
    31	
    32	function isValidDataUrl(url: string): boolean {
    33	  return /^data:image\/(png|jpeg|jpg|gif|svg\+xml|webp);base64,/.test(url);
    34	}
    35	
    36	function BrandStyleInjector({ brandData }: { brandData: { primaryColor?: string; logoBase64?: string } }) {
    37	  const safeColor = brandData.primaryColor && isValidCssColor(brandData.primaryColor)
    38	    ? brandData.primaryColor
    39	    : "#b8860b";
    40	  const safeLogo = brandData.logoBase64 && isValidDataUrl(brandData.logoBase64)
    41	    ? brandData.logoBase64
    42	    : null;
    43	
    44	  const css = `
    45	    :root { --brand-gold: ${safeColor} !important; }
    46	    .bg-brand-gold, .progress-segment.active, .gauge-bar-fill.score-warning {
    47	      background-color: ${safeColor} !important;
    48	    }
    49	    .text-brand-gold, .price-token { color: ${safeColor} !important; }
    50	    .border-brand-gold { border-color: ${safeColor} !important; }

    52	      background-image: url(${safeLogo}) !important;

    61	      }
    62	    }

    86	export default function ProspectLanding() {
    87	  const { slug } = useParams<{ slug: string }>();
    88	  const [searchParams] = useSearchParams();
    89	  const isPrint = searchParams.get('print') === 'true';
    90	
    91	  const [scanComplete, setScanComplete] = useState(isPrint);
    92	  const [currentStage, setCurrentStage] = useState(0);
    93	  const hasIncremented = useRef(false);
    94	
    95	  const isMock = slug === 'mock-prospect';
    96	
    97	  const { data, isLoading } = trpc.prospects.getBySlug.useQuery(
    98	    { slug: slug || '' },
    99	    { enabled: !!slug && !isMock }
   100	  );
   101	
   102	  const { data: brandData } = trpc.branding.getSettings.useQuery();
   103	
   104	  const incrementViews = trpc.prospects.incrementViews.useMutation();
   105	
   106	  const prospectId = isMock ? 5 : (data?.prospect?.id as number ?? 0);
   107	  const tracker = useActivityTracker(prospectId);
   108	  const trackerRef = useRef(tracker);
   109	  useEffect(() => {
   110	    trackerRef.current = tracker;
   111	  }, [tracker]);
   112	
   113	  const handleScanComplete = useCallback(() => {
   114	    setScanComplete(true);
   115	  }, []);
   116	
   117	  const handleCopyQA = useCallback((text: string) => {
   118	    trackerRef.current.trackEvent('copy_qa', { text: text.slice(0, 100) }, 10);
   119	  }, []);
   120	
   121	  const handleDownloadPPC = useCallback(() => {
   122	    trackerRef.current.trackEvent('download_ppc', {}, 15);
   123	  }, []);
   124

   126	    if (slug && !isMock && incrementViews && !hasIncremented.current) {
   127	      hasIncremented.current = true;
   128	      incrementViews.mutate({ slug });
   129	    }
   130	  }, [slug, incrementViews, isMock]);
   131	
   132	  useEffect(() => {
   133	    if (!scanComplete) return;
   134	
   135	    const stageNames = [
   136	      'hero', 'autopsy', 'bleed', 'simulator', 'transform',
   137	      'free-qas', 'ppc-planner', 'bundling', 'roadmap', 'proof', 'book',
   138	    ];

   141	      'stage-hero',

   143	      'stage-bleed',
   144	      'stage-simulator',
   145	      'stage-transform',

   151	      'stage-book',
   152	    ];
   153	
   154	    const handleScroll = () => {
   155	      const scrollY = window.scrollY + window.innerHeight * 0.4;
   156	
   157	      for (let i = stageIds.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   158	        const el = document.getElementById(stageIds[i]);
   159	        if (el && el.offsetTop <= scrollY) {
   160	          if (i !== currentStage) {
   161	            setCurrentStage(i);
   162	            trackerRef.current.trackScrollStage(i, stageNames[i]);
   163	          }
   164	          break;
   165	        }
   166	      }
   167	    };
   168	
   169	    window.addEventListener('scroll', handleScroll, { passive: true });
   170	    handleScroll();
   171	
   172	    return () => window.removeEventListener('scroll', handleScroll);
   173	  }, [scanComplete, currentStage]);
   174	
   175	  const scrollToBooking = () => {
   176	    const el = document.getElementById('stage-book');
   177	    if (el) el.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
   178	  };
   179	
   180	  if (isLoading && !isMock) {
   181	    return <SkeletonLoader />;
   182	  }
   183	
   184	  if (!data && !isMock) {

     6

    10	// Optional API-key authentication. If API_KEY env var is set, all mutations
    11	// and sensitive queries require it via x-api-key header or ?apiKey query param.
    12	const API_KEY = process.env.API_KEY;
    13	
    14	export const apiKeyProcedure = t.procedure.use(async ({ getRawInput, path, next }) => {
    15	  if (!API_KEY) {
    16	    // Auth not configured — allow through (backward compatible)
    17	    return next();
    18	  }
    19	
    20	  // Health check and public read endpoints stay open
    21	  const publicPaths = [
    22	    "health",
    23	    "prospects.getBySlug",
    24	    "prospects.incrementViews",
    25	    "branding.getSettings",
    26	    "agents.getStatus",
    27	    "agents.getLatestJob",
    28	    "catalogGraph.getGraph",
    29	    "rufusTracker.getSOVHistory",
    30	  ];
    31	  if (publicPaths.includes(path)) {
    32	    return next();
    33	  }
    34	
    35	  // Extract key from input payload for now (headers require custom context factory)
    36	  const rawInput = await getRawInput();
    37	  const input = rawInput as Record<string, unknown> | undefined;
    38	  const providedKey = input?.apiKey || input?.api_key;
    39	  if (providedKey !== API_KEY) {
    40	    throw new TRPCError({
    41	      code: "UNAUTHORIZED",
    42	      message: "Invalid or missing API key",
    43	    });
    44	  }
    45	
    46	  return next();
    47	});
    48	
    49	/**
    50	 * Converts our stub-style router objects to real tRPC routers.
    51	 * Stub objects have: { type: 'query'|'mutation', input: ZodSchema, resolve: fn }
    52	 */
    53	export function stubToRouter(stub: Record<string, unknown>) {
    54	  const converted: Record<string, unknown> = {};
    55	
    56	  for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(stub)) {
    57	    if (value === null || typeof value !== "object") {
    58	      converted[key] = value;
    59	      continue;
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    const v = value as Record<string, unknown>;
    63	
    64	    if (v.type === "query" && typeof v.resolve === "function") {
    65	      const proc = t.procedure;
    66	      if (v.input && v.input instanceof z.ZodType) {
    67	        converted[key] = proc.input(v.input as z.ZodTypeAny).query(v.resolve as any);
    68	      } else {
    69	        converted[key] = proc.query(v.resolve as any);
    70	      }
    71	    } else if (v.type === "mutation" && typeof v.resolve === "function") {
    72	      const proc = t.procedure;
    73	      if (v.input && v.input instanceof z.ZodType) {
    74	        converted[key] = proc.input(v.input as z.ZodTypeAny).mutation(v.resolve as any);
    75	      } else {
    76	        converted[key] = proc.mutation(v.resolve as any);
    77	      }
    78	    } else {
    79	      // Nested router object
    80	      converted[key] = stubToRouter(v as Record<string, unknown>);
    81	    }
    82	  }
    83	
    84	  return converted;
    85	}

     1	import { db } from "../db/client.js";
     2	import type { Job, JobOpts, JobQueue } from "./types.js";
     3	
     4	function generateId(): string {
     5	  return `${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 11)}`;
     6	}
     7	
     8	export class SQLiteJobQueue implements JobQueue {
     9	  private queueName: string;
    10	
    11	  constructor(queueName: string) {
    12	    this.queueName = queueName;
    13	  }
    14	
    15	  async add(name: string, data: unknown, opts: JobOpts = {}): Promise<Job> {
    16	    const id = generateId();
    17	    const now = Date.now();
    18	    const delay = opts.delay ?? 0;
    19	    const maxAttempts = opts.maxAttempts ?? 3;
    20	
    21	    db.prepare(
    22	      `INSERT INTO jobs (id, queue, name, dataJSON, optsJSON, delay, timestamp, maxAttempts, status)
    23	       VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, 'pending')`
    24	    ).run(
    25	      id,
    26	      this.queueName,
    27	      name,
    28	      JSON.stringify(data),
    29	      JSON.stringify(opts),
    30	      delay,
    31	      now,
    32	      maxAttempts
    33	    );
    34	
    35	    return {
    36	      id,
    37	      name,
    38	      data,
    39	      opts,
    40	      progress: 0,
    41	      attempts: 0,
    42	      maxAttempts,
    43	      status: delay > 0 ? "delayed" : "pending",
    44	    };
    45	  }
    46	
    47	  async getJob(id: string): Promise<Job | null> {
    48	    const row = db.prepare("SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = ?").get(id) as
    49	      | Record<string, unknown>
    50	      | undefined;
    51	    if (!row) return null;
    52	    return this.hydrate(row);
    53	  }
    54	
    55	  async updateProgress(id: string, progress: number): Promise<void> {
    56	    db.prepare("UPDATE jobs SET progress = ? WHERE id = ?").run(progress, id);
    57	  }
    58	
    59	  /**
    60	   * Poll for the next pending job in this queue.
    61	   * Returns null if no job is ready.
    62	   */
    63	  pollNext(): Job | null {
    64	    const now = Date.now();
    65	    const row = db
    66	      .prepare(
    67	        `SELECT * FROM jobs
    68	         WHERE queue = ? AND status = 'pending' AND (delay = 0 OR timestamp + delay <= ?)
    69	         ORDER BY timestamp ASC
    70	         LIMIT 1`
    71	      )
    72	      .get(this.queueName, now) as Record<string, unknown> | undefined;
    73	
    74	    if (!row) return null;
    75	    return this.hydrate(row);
    76	  }
    77	
    78	  /**
    79	   * Mark a job as active (lock it for processing).
    80	   */

The graph shows `db` has the highest betweenness centrality (0.036) and `client.ts` is the #1 node by degree (39).\n\n### 1.1 Add Dependencies\n```bash\nnpm install drizzle-orm postgres pg\nnpm install -D drizzle-kit @types/pg\n```\n\n### 1.2 Create Schema-as-Code\n- Create `api/db/schema.ts` (new) using Drizzle's `pgTable` definitions\n- Map all existing SQLite tables to PostgreSQL equivalents\n- Use `serial`, `text`, `integer`, `real`, `timestamp`, `jsonb` appropriately\n- Replace `JSON.stringify` fields with `jsonb` columns (gaps, topIssues, strengths, etc.)\n- Keep `embeddingVector` as `text` for now (migrate to `vector` extension later)\n\n### 1.3 Create Connection Layer\n- `api/db/client.ts` → keep for backward compat during transition\n- Create `api/db/drizzle.ts`: exports `drizzle(pool)` instance\n- Create `api/db/migrate.ts`: runs Drizzle migrations via `drizzle-kit migrate`\n- Environment: `DATABASE_URL` (PostgreSQL connection string)\n\n### 1.4 Data Migration Script\n- Create `scripts/migrateSqliteToPostgres.ts`\n- Reads from existing SQLite, writes to PostgreSQL via Drizzle\n- Handles JSON serialization/deserialization for fields moving to `jsonb`\n- Idempotent (can be re-run safely)\n\n### 1.5 Verification\n- `npm run check` passes\n- Health check endpoint queries PostgreSQL\n- All existing tRPC endpoints still work (still using old `db` at this point)\n\n---\n\n## Phase 2: Repository Layer (Isolate the `db` God Node)\n\n**Why:** The graph shows `db` is imported by 23 files across 6 communities. We must reduce this to 1 (the repository layer).\n\n### 2.1 Create Repository Modules\nCreate `api/db/repositories/` with one module per domain:\n\n| Repository | Replaces Direct SQL In |\n|---|---|\n| `prospectRepository.ts` | `routers/prospects.ts`, `routers/analysis.ts`, scripts |\n| `listingRepository.ts` | `routers/scraper.ts`, `routers/analysis.ts`, `pipeline/stages.ts` |\n| `analysisRepository.ts` | `routers/analysis.ts` |\n| `bookingRepository.ts` | `routers/booking.ts` |\n| `activityRepository.ts` | `routers/prospects.ts` |\n| `pipelineRepository.ts` | `pipeline/engine.ts`, `pipeline/worker.ts` |\n| `brandRepository.ts` | `routers/branding.ts` |\n| `catalogRepository.ts` | `routers/catalogGraphRouter.ts` |\n| `rufusRepository.ts` | `routers/rufusTracker.ts` |\n\n### 2.2 Repository Interface Pattern\n```typescript\n// Each repository is a plain object with async functions\nexport const prospectRepository = {\n  async create(input: CreateProspectInput): Promise<ProspectRecord> { ... },\n  async getBySlug(slug: string): Promise<ProspectRecord | undefined> { ... },\n  async incrementViews(slug: string): Promise<void> { ... },\n  // etc.\n};\n```\n\n### 2.3 Migrate Callers Incrementally\nOrder: scripts first (lowest risk), then routers, then pipeline engine.\n- Replace `db.prepare(\"SELECT * FROM prospects ...\")` with `prospectRepository.getBySlug()`\n- Keep `withTransaction()` as a utility but move it to `api/db/transaction.ts`\n\n### 2.4 Target State\n- Only `api/db/repositories/*`, `api/db/migrations/*`, and `api/infra/queue.ts` import from the DB client\n- `db` node degree drops from 23 to ~5\n- `client.ts` degree drops from 39 to ~10 (types extracted in Phase 3)\n\n---\n\n## Phase 3: Extract Types & Decouple `client.ts`\n\n**Why:** `client.ts` is doing triple duty: connection factory, type definitions, and transaction utilities.\n\n### 3.1 Extract Types\n- Create `api/db/types.ts` containing all `*Record` interfaces\n- Update all imports across the codebase:\n  ```typescript\n  // Before\n  import type { ProspectRecord } from \"../db/client.js\";\n  // After\n  import type { ProspectRecord } from \"../db/types.js\";\n  ```\n\n### 3.2 Extract Transaction Utilities\n- Move `withTransaction()` and `withTransactionAsync()` to `api/db/transaction.ts`\n\n### 3.3 Clean Up `client.ts`\n- `client.ts` only exports the SQLite `db` instance (for backward compat) and the Drizzle `db` instance\n- Degree drops from 39 to ~6\n\n---\n\n## Phase 4: Service Layer (Decouple Routers from Business Logic)\n\n**Why:** Routers like `analysis.ts` (300 lines) mix tRPC boilerplate, SQL, copy generation, and score calculation. The graph shows `analysis.ts` has degree 17 with 6 cross-community links.\n\n### 4.1 Create Domain Services\nCreate `api/services/domain/` (separate from existing `api/services/` which holds external integrations):\n\n| Service | Responsibilities |\n|---|---|\n| `prospectService.ts` | Create prospect, record activity, trigger webhooks |\n| `analysisService.ts` | Run pipeline, extract results, persist analysis, generate copy |\n| `listingService.ts` | Scrape, store, and retrieve listings |\n| `bookingService.ts` | Handle booking CRUD |\n| `pipelineService.ts` | Orchestrate job creation, status checks, retries |\n\n### 4.2 Router Refactoring Pattern\n```typescript\n// Before: router contains SQL + business logic\nexport const analysisRouter = router({\n  run: publicProcedure.input(...).mutation(async ({ input }) => {\n    const listing = db.prepare(\"SELECT ...\").get(...) as ListingRecord;\n    // 50 lines of business logic ...\n  })\n});\n\n// After: router is a thin adapter\nexport const analysisRouter = router({\n  run: publicProcedure.input(...).mutation(async ({ input }) => {\n    return analysisService.run(input.listingId);\n  })\n});\n```\n\n### 4.3 Target State\n- No router imports `db` directly\n- No router contains raw SQL\n- Business logic is testable in isolation\n\n---\n\n## Phase 5: Pipeline Decoupling\n\n**Why:** `stages.ts` (degree 34, 16 cross-community) imports 7 agent classes, `db`, `copywriter`, `rufusSimulator`, `logger`, and `eventBus`. It is the #2 bridge node.\n\n### 5.1 Split `stages.ts` Into Three Files\n\n**`api/pipeline/types.ts`** (already exists, but clean up):\n- Keep `StageName`, `StageDefinition`, `StageOutput`, `PipelineJob`, `StageContext`, `StageExecutor`\n- **Remove** the import from `../agents/types.js` — replace agent-specific types with generic `unknown` or define minimal pipeline-local interfaces\n\n**`api/pipeline/definitions.ts`** (new):\n- Only exports `STAGE_ORDER` — pure data, zero imports\n```typescript\nexport const STAGE_ORDER: StageDefinition[] = [\n  { name: \"fetch\", dependencies: [] },\n  { name: \"preprocess\", dependencies: [\"fetch\"] },\n  // ...\n];\n```\n\n**`api/pipeline/executors.ts`** (new):\n- Contains the `stageExecutors` array\n- Imports agents, services, db (via repositories after Phase 2)\n- This is the only file that knows how to run stages\n\n### 5.2 Remove `db` Access from Stage Executors\n- The `embedding` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"UPDATE listings SET embeddingVector ...\")`\n- Move this to `listingService.updateEmbedding()`\n- The `optimize` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"SELECT firstName, lastName ...\")`\n- Move this to `prospectService.getForPipeline(ctx.prospectId)`\n\n### 5.3 Target State\n- `engine.ts` only imports `STAGE_ORDER` from `definitions.ts` and `stageExecutors` from `executors.ts`\n- `definitions.ts` has **zero** cross-community links\n- `engine.ts` degree drops from 22 to ~12\n\n---\n\n## Phase 6: Frontend Monolith Cleanup\n\n**Why:** `ProspectLanding.tsx` imports from 8 communities, has 27 edges, and is 393 lines.\n\n### 6.1 Extract Sub-Components Already in the File\n- `BrandStyleInjector` → `src/components/landing/BrandStyleInjector.tsx`\n- `SkeletonLoader` → `src/components/landing/SkeletonLoader.tsx`\n\n### 6.2 Create a Landing Page Composer\n- `src/components/landing/LandingPageComposer.tsx`\n- Accepts `prospect: ProspectData` and `brandData`\n- Renders all sections in order\n- `ProspectLanding.tsx` becomes a thin wrapper:\n  - Data fetching (tRPC)\n  - Scroll tracking\n  - Delegates rendering to `LandingPageComposer`\n\n### 6.3 Target State\n- `ProspectLanding.tsx` drops from 393 lines to ~80 lines\n- Degree drops from 27 to ~12\n\n---\n\n## Phase 7: Auth, Quality, and Testing\n\n### 7.1 Authentication\n- Replace stub `apiKeyProcedure` with verifies JWT and attaches `user` to context\n- Protect admin routes (`AdminDashboard.tsx`) and mutation endpoints\n\n### 7.2 Fix Lint Errors\n- 61 ESLint errors currently exist\n- Bulk-fix `any` types in tRPC context and pipeline types\n- Fix `setState` in `useEffect` violations\n- Remove unused variables\n- Add `lint:fix` script if not present\n\n### 7.3 Testing Infrastructure\n```bash\nnpm install -D vitest @vitest/ui @testing-library/react @testing-library/jest-dom jsdom\nnpm install -D @playwright/test\n```\n\n**Unit tests:**\n- `api/db/repositories/*.test.ts` — repository logic with in-memory PostgreSQL (via `pg-mem` or testcontainers)\n- `api/services/domain/*.test.ts` — business logic\n\n**Integration tests:**\n- `api/routers/*.test.ts` — tRPC router tests using `createCallerFactory`\n\n**E2E tests:**\n- `e2e/landing.spec.ts` — Playwright: load landing page, verify sections\n- `e2e/pipeline.spec.ts` — trigger analysis, verify job completion\n\n### 7.4 Prune Orphaned Code\n- Audit the 245 orphaned code nodes\n- Delete unused interfaces (`OptimizationReport` if unused, duplicate types, etc.)\n- Remove `api/services/optimization.ts` if it remains a stub\n\n---\n\n## Rollback & Safety Strategy\n\n- **Feature flags:** Each phase is gated by a commit. Additionally, we must implement the **Execute → Evaluate → Retry** pattern.\n\n### 5.1 Split `stages.ts` Into Three Files\n\n**`api/pipeline/types.ts`** (already exists, but clean up):\n- Keep `StageName`, `StageDefinition`, `StageOutput`, `PipelineJob`, `StageContext`, `StageExecutor`\n- **Remove** the import from `../agents/types.js` — replace agent-specific types with generic `unknown` or define minimal pipeline-local interfaces\n\n**`api/pipeline/definitions.ts`** (new):\n- Only exports `STAGE_ORDER` — pure data, zero imports\n```typescript\nexport const STAGE_ORDER: StageDefinition[] = [\n  { name: \"fetch\", dependencies: [] },\n  { name: \"preprocess\", dependencies: [\"fetch\"] },\n  // ...\n];\n```\n\n**`api/pipeline/executors.ts`** (new):\n- Contains the `stageExecutors` array\n- Imports agents, services, db (via repositories after Phase 2)\n- This is the only file that knows how to run stages\n\n### 5.2 Implement Subagent Evaluator Pattern\n\nCreate `api/agents/evaluators/` with one evaluator per execution agent:\n\n| Executor | Evaluator | Checks |\n|---|---|---|\n| `ApifyFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | ASIN data completeness, required fields present, schema valid |\n| `ListingFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | Same as above |\n| `PreprocessorAgent` | `PreprocessEvaluator` | Text cleaned, no HTML artifacts, structure preserved |\n| `EmbeddingGeneratorAgent` | `EmbeddingEvaluator` | Vector length correct (1536), no NaN values, normalized |\n| `SemanticAnalyzerAgent` | `SemanticEvaluator` | Gap scores in [0,1], priorities valid, recommendations non-empty |\n| `ContentOptimizerAgent` | `OptimizeEvaluator` | Title < 200 chars, 5 bullets, description valid HTML, QAs have answers |\n| `CompetitorAnalystAgent` | `CompetitorEvaluator` | Competitor count > 0, scores in range, ASINs valid |\n\n**Evaluator interface:**\n```typescript\nexport interface Evaluator<T> {\n  evaluate(input: unknown, output: T): Promise<{\n    passed: boolean;\n    score: number; // 0-100\n    issues: string[];\n    suggestions: string[];\n  }>;\n}\n```\n\n**Stage executor loop:**\n```typescript\nasync function executeWithEvaluation<T>(\n  executor: () => Promise<T>,\n  evaluator: Evaluator<T>,\n  input: unknown,\n  maxAttempts = 3\n): Promise<T> {\n  for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxAttempts; attempt++) {\n    const output = await executor();\n    const review = await evaluator.evaluate(input, output);\n    if (review.passed) return output;\n    if (attempt === maxAttempts) {\n      throw new Error(`Stage failed evaluation after ${maxAttempts} attempts: ${review.issues.join(\"; \")}`);\n    }\n    // Log feedback for retry\n    logger.warn(\"Stage evaluation failed, retrying\", { attempt, issues: review.issues });\n  }\n  throw new Error(\"Unreachable\");\n}\n```\n\n**Note:** The current `ReviewerAgent` is a generic post-hoc reviewer. The new evaluators are **per-stage, schema-aware, and triggered automatically** within the pipeline loop. `ReviewerAgent` can be deleted or repurposed as a final quality gate after all stages complete.\n\n### 5.3 Remove `db` Access from Stage Executors\n- The `embedding` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"UPDATE listings SET embeddingVector ...\")`\n- Move this to `listingService.updateEmbedding()`\n- The `optimize` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"SELECT firstName, lastName ...\")`\n- Move this to `prospectService.getForPipeline(ctx.prospectId)`\n\n### 5.4 Target State\n- `engine.ts` only imports `STAGE_ORDER` from `definitions.ts` and `stageExecutors` from `executors.ts`\n- `definitions.ts` has **zero** cross-community links\n- `engine.ts` degree drops from 22 to ~12\n- Each stage has a dedicated evaluator in `api/agents/evaluators/`\n- Pipeline failures include specific evaluator feedback in the error log"
    }
  ]
}

     1	# Optimus Rufus — Upgrade & Structural Optimization Plan
     2	
     3	## Goal
     4	Eliminate the architectural chokepoints identified by the knowledge graph (`db` god node, 154 cross-community links, 290 orphaned nodes) while migrating from ephemeral SQLite to persistent PostgreSQL + Drizzle ORM. **Remove Amazon SP-API dependency entirely** — it is undocumented in the active codebase and causes integration friction. **Restructure the AI pipeline so every agent execution is followed by an evaluator subagent review**.
     5	
     6	## Approach
     7	Incremental refactoring in 7 phases. Each phase is designed to be committable independently, with the app remaining functional after every phase. No big-bang rewrites. During plan execution, each phase will be delegated to a subagent, and each subagent will spawn a reviewer subagent to validate its output before the parent agent accepts the work.
     8	
     9	## Key Architectural Decisions
    10	
    11	### 1. No Amazon SP-API
    12	- Remove all SP-API references from documentation, env vars, and architecture
    13	- Primary data sources: **Apify scraper** + **Rainforest API** (already implemented)
    14	- Listing enrichment via LLM-based inference rather than seller central APIs
    15	
    16	### 2. Subagent Evaluation Pattern
    17	Every pipeline stage will follow an **Execute → Evaluate → (Retry if needed)** loop:
    18	
    19	```
    20	StageExecutor
    21	  ├─ ExecutionSubagent (does the work)
    22	  └─ EvaluationSubagent (reviews the output)
    23	       ├─ PASS → stage completes
    24	       └─ FAIL → ExecutionSubagent retries with feedback
    25	```
    26	
    27	- Each `StageExecutor` delegates to an `ExecutionSubagent` class
    28	- Each `ExecutionSubagent` has a paired `EvaluationSubagent` class
    29	- The evaluator checks output quality, completeness, and schema validity
    30	- After 3 failed evaluations, the stage fails with accumulated feedback
    31	- This replaces the current monolithic `ReviewerAgent` with per-stage evaluators
    32	
    33	---
    34	
    35	## Phase 1: Drizzle ORM + PostgreSQL Foundation
    36	
    37	**Why first:** Everything else depends on the database layer. The graph shows `db` has the highest betweenness centrality (0.036) and `client.ts` is the #1 node by degree (39).
    38	
    39	### 1.1 Add Dependencies
    40	```bash
    41	npm install drizzle-orm postgres pg
    42	npm install -D drizzle-kit @types/pg
    43	```
    44	
    45	### 1.2 Create Schema-as-Code
    46	- Create `api/db/schema.ts` (new) using Drizzle's `pgTable` definitions
    47	- Map all existing SQLite tables to PostgreSQL equivalents
    48	- Use `serial`, `text`, `integer`, `real`, `timestamp`, `jsonb` appropriately
    49	- Replace `JSON.stringify` fields with `jsonb` columns (gaps, topIssues, strengths, etc.)
    50	- Keep `embeddingVector` as `text` for now (migrate to `vector` extension later)
    51

    56	- Environment: `DATABASE_URL` (PostgreSQL connection string)

    79	## Phase 2: Repository Layer (Isolate the `db` God Node)
    80	
    81	**Why:** The graph shows `db` is imported by 23 files across 6 communities. We must reduce this to 1 (the repository layer).

    85

    87	|---|---|
    88	| `prospectRepository.ts` | `routers/prospects.ts`, `routers/analysis.ts`, scripts |

    96	| `rufusRepository.ts` | `routers/rufusTracker.ts` |
    97	
    98	**Execution model:** A subagent will implement each repository. After each repository is written, a reviewer subagent will verify it against the original SQL it replaces (query logic, parameter binding, return shapes).
    99	
   100	### 2.2 Repository Interface Pattern
   101	```typescript

   104	  async create(input: CreateProspectInput): Promise<ProspectRecord> { ... },
   105	  async getBySlug(slug: string): Promise<ProspectRecord | undefined> { ... },

   107	  // etc.
   108	};
   109	```

   167	    // 50 lines of business logic ...
   168	  })
   169	});
   170

   175	  })
   176	});
   177	```

// 0-100\n    issues: string[];\n    suggestions: string[];\n  }>;\n}\n```\n\n**Stage executor loop:**\n```typescript\nasync function executeWithEvaluation<T>(\n  executor: () => Promise<T>,\n  evaluator: Evaluator<T>,\n  input: unknown,\n  maxAttempts = 3\n): Promise<T> {\n  for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxAttempts; attempt++) {\n    const output = await executor();\n    const review = await evaluator.evaluate(input, output);\n    if (review.passed) return output;\n    if (attempt === maxAttempts) {\n      throw new Error(`Stage failed evaluation after ${maxAttempts} attempts: ${review.issues.join(\"; \")}`);\n    }\n    // Log feedback for retry\n    logger.warn(\"Stage evaluation failed, retrying\", { attempt, issues: review.issues });\n  }\n  throw new Error(\"Unreachable\");\n}\n```\n\n**Note:** The current `ReviewerAgent` is a generic post-hoc reviewer. The new evaluators are **per-stage, schema-aware, and triggered automatically** within the pipeline loop. `ReviewerAgent` can be deleted or repurposed as a final quality gate after all stages complete.\n\n### 5.3 Remove `db` Access from Stage Executors\n- The `embedding` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"UPDATE listings SET embeddingVector ...\")`\n- Move this to `listingService.updateEmbedding()`\n- The `optimize` stage currently does: `db.prepare(\"SELECT firstName, lastName ...\")`\n- Move this to `prospectService.getForPipeline(ctx.prospectId)`\n\n### 5.4 Target State\n- `engine.ts` only imports `STAGE_ORDER` from `definitions.ts` and `stageExecutors` from `executors.ts`\n- `definitions.ts` has **zero** cross-community links\n- `engine.ts` degree drops from 22 to ~12\n- Each stage has a dedicated evaluator in `api/agents/evaluators/`\n- Pipeline failures include specific evaluator feedback in the error log"
    }
  ]
}

     1	# Optimus Rufus — Upgrade & Structural Optimization Plan
     2	
     3	## Goal
     4	Eliminate the architectural chokepoints identified by the knowledge graph (`db` god node, 154 cross-community links, 290 orphaned nodes) while migrating from ephemeral SQLite to persistent PostgreSQL + Drizzle ORM. **Remove Amazon SP-API dependency entirely** — it is undocumented in the active codebase and causes integration friction. **Restructure the AI pipeline so every agent execution is followed by an evaluator subagent review**.
     5	
     6	## Approach
     7	Incremental refactoring in 7 phases. Each phase is designed to be committable independently, with the app remaining functional after every phase. No big-bang rewrites. During plan execution, each phase will be delegated to a subagent, and each subagent will spawn a reviewer subagent to validate its output before the parent agent accepts the work.
     8	
     9	## Key Architectural Decisions
    10	
    11	### 1. No Amazon SP-API
    12	- Remove all SP-API references from documentation, env vars, and architecture
    13	- Primary data sources: **Apify scraper** + **Rainforest API** (already implemented)
    14	- Listing enrichment via LLM-based inference rather than seller central APIs
    15	
    16	### 2. Subagent Evaluation Pattern
    17	Every pipeline stage will follow an **Execute → Evaluate → (Retry if needed)** loop:
    18	
    19	```
    20	StageExecutor
    21	  ├─ ExecutionSubagent (does the work)
    22	  └─ EvaluationSubagent (reviews the output)
    23	       ├─ PASS → stage completes
    24	       └─ FAIL → ExecutionSubagent retries with feedback
    25	```
    26	
    27	- Each `StageExecutor` delegates to an `ExecutionSubagent` class
    28	- Each `ExecutionSubagent` has a paired `EvaluationSubagent` class
    29	- The evaluator checks output quality, completeness, and schema validity
    30	- After 3 failed evaluations, the stage fails with accumulated feedback
    31	- This replaces the current monolithic `ReviewerAgent` with per-stage evaluators
    32	
    33	---
    34	
    35	## Phase 1: Drizzle ORM + PostgreSQL Foundation
    36	
    37	**Why first:** Everything else depends on the database layer. The graph shows `db` has the highest betweenness centrality (0.036) and `client.ts` is the #1 node by degree (39).
    38	
    39	### 1.1 Add Dependencies
    40	```bash
    41	npm install drizzle-orm postgres pg
    42	npm install -D drizzle-kit @types/pg
    43	```
    44	
    45	### 1.2 Create Schema-as-Code
    46	- Create `api/db/schema.ts` (new) using Drizzle's `pgTable` definitions
    47	- Map all existing SQLite tables to PostgreSQL equivalents
    48	- Use `serial`, `text`, `integer`, `real`, `timestamp`, `jsonb` appropriately
    49	- Replace `JSON.stringify` fields with `jsonb` columns (gaps, topIssues, strengths, etc.)
    50	- Keep `embeddingVector` as `text` for now (migrate to `vector` extension later)
    51	
    52	### 1.3 Create Connection Layer
    53	- `api/db/client.ts` → keep for backward compat during transition
    54	- Create `api/db/drizzle.ts`: exports `drizzle(pool)` instance
    55	- Create `api/db/migrate.ts`: runs Drizzle migrations via `drizzle-kit migrate`
    56	- Environment: `DATABASE_URL` (PostgreSQL connection string)
    57	
    58	### 1.4 Remove SP-API Artifacts
    59	- Delete `docs/02-research/amazon-sp-api.md` if it exists
    60	- Remove `AMAZON_CLIENT_ID`, `AMAZON_CLIENT_SECRET`, `AMAZON_APP_ID` from `.env.example`
    61	- Remove SP-API references from `docs/04-architecture/technical-architecture.md`
    62	- Delete `api/services/spapi.ts` if it is a stub or unused
    63	- Update `docs/README.md` to state: "Listing data is sourced via Apify and Rainforest API scraping; no SP-API credentials required"
    64	
    65	### 1.5 Data Migration Script
    66	- Create `scripts/migrateSqliteToPostgres.ts`
    67	- Reads from existing SQLite, writes to PostgreSQL via Drizzle
    68	- Handles JSON serialization/deserialization for fields moving to `jsonb`
    69	- Idempotent (can be re-run safely)
    70	
    71	### 1.6 Verification
    72	- `npm run check` passes
    73	- Health check endpoint queries PostgreSQL
    74	- All existing tRPC endpoints still work (still using old `db` at this point)
    75	- `npm run lint` shows no new errors
    76	
    77	---
    78	
    79	## Phase 2: Repository Layer (Isolate the `db` God Node)
    80	
    81	**Why:** The graph shows `db` is imported by 23 files across 6 communities. We must reduce this to 1 (the repository layer).
    82	
    83	### 2.1 Create Repository Modules
    84	Create `api/db/repositories/` with one module per domain:
    85	
    86	| Repository | Replaces Direct SQL In |
    87	|---|---|
    88	| `prospectRepository.ts` | `routers/prospects.ts`, `routers/analysis.ts`, scripts |
    89	| `listingRepository.ts` | `routers/scraper.ts`, `routers/analysis.ts`, `pipeline/stages.ts` |
    90	| `analysisRepository.ts` | `routers/analysis.ts` |
    91	| `bookingRepository.ts` | `routers/booking.ts` |
    92	| `activityRepository.ts` | `routers/prospects.ts` |
    93	| `pipelineRepository.ts` | `pipeline/engine.ts`, `pipeline/worker.ts` |
    94	| `brandRepository.ts` | `routers/branding.ts` |
    95	| `catalogRepository.ts` | `routers/catalogGraphRouter.ts` |
    96	| `rufusRepository.ts` | `routers/rufusTracker.ts` |
    97	
    98	**Execution model:** A subagent will implement each repository. After each repository is written, a reviewer subagent will verify it against the original SQL it replaces (query logic, parameter binding, return shapes).
    99	
   100	### 2.2 Repository Interface Pattern
   101	```typescript
   102	// Each repository is a plain object with async functions
   103	export const prospectRepository = {
   104	  async create(input: CreateProspectInput): Promise<ProspectRecord> { ... },
   105	  async getBySlug(slug: string): Promise<ProspectRecord | undefined> { ... },
   106	  async incrementViews(slug: string): Promise<void> { ... },
   107	  // etc.
   108	};
   109	```
   110	
   111	### 2.3 Migrate Callers Incrementally
   112	Order: scripts first (lowest risk), then routers, then pipeline engine.
   113	- Replace `db.prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects ...")` with `prospectRepository.getBySlug()`
   114	- Keep `withTransaction()` as a utility but move it to `api/db/transaction.ts`
   115	
   116	### 2.4 Target State
   117	- Only `api/db/repositories/*`, `api/db/migrations/*`, and `api/infra/queue.ts` import from the DB client
   118	- `db` node degree drops from 23 to ~5
   119	- `client.ts` degree drops from 39 to ~10 (types extracted in Phase 3)
   120	
   121	---
   122	
   123	## Phase 3: Extract Types & Decouple `client.ts`
   124	
   125	**Why:** `client.ts` is doing triple duty: connection factory, type definitions, and transaction utilities.
   126	
   127	### 3.1 Extract Types
   128	- Create `api/db/types.ts` containing all `*Record` interfaces
   129	- Update all imports across the codebase:
   130	  ```typescript
   131	  // Before
   132	  import type { ProspectRecord } from "../db/client.js";
   133	  // After
   134	  import type { ProspectRecord } from "../db/types.js";
   135	  ```
   136	
   137	### 3.2 Extract Transaction Utilities
   138	- Move `withTransaction()` and `withTransactionAsync()` to `api/db/transaction.ts`
   139	
   140	### 3.3 Clean Up `client.ts`
   141	- `client.ts` only exports the SQLite `db` instance (for backward compat) and the Drizzle `db` instance
   142	- Degree drops from 39 to ~6
   143	
   144	---
   145	
   146	## Phase 4: Service Layer (Decouple Routers from Business Logic)
   147	
   148	**Why:** Routers like `analysis.ts` (300 lines) mix tRPC boilerplate, SQL, copy generation, and score calculation. The graph shows `analysis.ts` has degree 17 with 6 cross-community links.
   149	
   150	### 4.1 Create Domain Services
   151	Create `api/services/domain/` (separate from existing `api/services/` which holds external integrations):
   152	
   153	| Service | Responsibilities |
   154	|---|---|
   155	| `prospectService.ts` | Create prospect, record activity, trigger webhooks |
   156	| `analysisService.ts` | Run pipeline, extract results, persist analysis, generate copy |
   157	| `listingService.ts` | Scrape (via Apify/Rainforest), store, and retrieve listings. No SP-API. |
   158	| `bookingService.ts` | Handle booking CRUD |
   159	| `pipelineService.ts` | Orchestrate job creation, status checks, retries |
   160	
   161	### 4.2 Router Refactoring Pattern
   162	```typescript
   163	// Before: router contains SQL + business logic
   164	export const analysisRouter = router({
   165	  run: publicProcedure.input(...).mutation(async ({ input }) => {
   166	    const listing = db.prepare("SELECT ...").get(...) as ListingRecord;
   167	    // 50 lines of business logic ...
   168	  })
   169	});
   170	
   171	// After: router is a thin adapter
   172	export const analysisRouter = router({
   173	  run: publicProcedure.input(...).mutation(async ({ input }) => {
   174	    return analysisService.run(input.listingId);
   175	  })
   176	});
   177	```
   178	
   179	### 4.3 Target State
   180	- No router imports `db` directly
   181	- No router contains raw SQL
   182	- Business logic is testable in isolation
   183	- `listingService.ts` explicitly documents: "We use Apify and Rainforest API for data fetching. SP-API is not used."
   184	
   185	---
   186	
   187	## Phase 5: Pipeline Decoupling + Subagent Evaluator Architecture
   188	
   189	**Why:** `stages.ts` (degree 34, 16 cross-community) imports 7 agent classes, `db`, `copywriter`, `rufusSimulator`, `logger`, and `eventBus`. It is the #2 bridge node. We also must implement the **Execute → Evaluate → Retry** pattern for every stage.
   190	
   191	### 5.1 Split `stages.ts` Into Three Files
   192	
   193	**`api/pipeline/types.ts`** (already exists, but clean up):
   194	- Keep `StageName`, `StageDefinition`, `StageOutput`, `PipelineJob`, `StageContext`, `StageExecutor`
   195	- **Remove** the import from `../agents/types.js` — replace agent-specific types with generic `unknown` or define minimal pipeline-local interfaces
   196	
   197	**`api/pipeline/definitions.ts`** (new):
   198	- Only exports `STAGE_ORDER` — pure data, zero imports
   199	```typescript
   200	export const STAGE_ORDER: StageDefinition[] = [
   201	  { name: "fetch", dependencies: [] },
   202	  { name: "preprocess", dependencies: ["fetch"] },
   203	  // ...
   204	];
   205	```
   206	
   207	**`api/pipeline/executors.ts`** (new):
   208	- Contains the `stageExecutors` array
   209	- Imports agents, evaluators, services
   210	- This is the only file that knows how to run stages
   211	
   212	### 5.2 Implement Subagent Evaluator Pattern
   213	
   214	Create `api/agents/evaluators/` with one evaluator per execution agent:
   215	
   216	| Executor | Evaluator | Checks |
   217	|---|---|---|
   218	| `ApifyFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | ASIN data completeness, required fields present, schema valid |
   219	| `ListingFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | Same as above |
   220	| `PreprocessorAgent` | `PreprocessEvaluator` | Text cleaned, no HTML artifacts, structure preserved |
   221	| `EmbeddingGeneratorAgent` | `EmbeddingEvaluator` | Vector length correct (1536), no NaN values, normalized |
   222	| `SemanticAnalyzerAgent` | `SemanticEvaluator` | Gap scores in [0,1], priorities valid, recommendations non-empty |
   223	| `ContentOptimizerAgent` | `OptimizeEvaluator` | Title < 200 chars, 5 bullets, description valid HTML, QAs have answers |
   224	| `CompetitorAnalystAgent` | `CompetitorEvaluator` | Competitor count > 0, scores in range, ASINs valid |
   225	
   226	**Evaluator interface:**
   227	```typescript
   228	export interface Evaluator<T> {
   229	  evaluate(input: unknown, output: T): Promise<{
   230	    passed: boolean;
   231	    score: number; // 0-100
   232	    issues: string[];
   233	    suggestions: string[];
   234	  }>;
   235	}
   236	```
   237	
   238	**Stage executor loop:**
   239	```typescript
   240	async function executeWithEvaluation<T>(
   241	  executor: () => Promise<T>,
   242	  evaluator: Evaluator<T>,
   243	  input: unknown,
   244	  maxAttempts = 3
   245	): Promise<T> {
   246	  for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxAttempts; attempt++) {
   247	    const output = await executor();
   248	    const review = await evaluator.evaluate(input, output);
   249	    if (review.passed) return output;
   250	    if (attempt === maxAttempts) {
   251	      throw new Error(`Stage failed evaluation after ${maxAttempts} attempts: ${review.issues.join("; ")}`);
   252	    }
   253	    // Log feedback for retry
   254	    logger.warn("Stage evaluation failed, retrying", { attempt, issues: review.issues });
   255	  }
   256	  throw new Error("Unreachable");
   257	}
   258	```
   259	
   260	**Note:** The current `ReviewerAgent` is a generic post-hoc reviewer. The new evaluators are **per-stage, schema-aware, and triggered automatically** within the pipeline loop. `ReviewerAgent` can be deleted or repurposed as a final quality gate after all stages complete.
   261	
   262	### 5.3 Remove `db` Access from Stage Executors
   263	- The `embedding` stage currently does: `db.prepare("UPDATE listings SET embeddingVector ...")`
   264	- Move this to `listingService.updateEmbedding()`
   265	- The `optimize` stage currently does: `db.prepare("SELECT firstName, lastName ...")`
   266	- Move this to `prospectService.getForPipeline(ctx.prospectId)`
   267	
   268	### 5.4 Target State
   269	- `engine.ts` only imports `STAGE_ORDER` from `definitions.ts` and `stageExecutors` from `executors.ts`
   270	- `definitions.ts` has **zero** cross-community links
   271	- `engine.ts` degree drops from 22 to ~12
   272	- Each stage has a dedicated evaluator in `api/agents/evaluators/`
   273	- Pipeline failures include specific evaluator feedback in the error log
   274	
   275	---

   301	
   302	### 7.1 Authentication

   315	
   316	### 7.3 Testing Infrastructure
   317	```bash
   318	npm install -D vitest @vitest/ui @testing-library/react @testing-library/jest-dom jsdom
   319	npm install -D @playwright/test
   320	```
   321	
   322	**Unit tests:**

   340	## Execution Model: Subagent Delegation
   341	
   342	Each phase of this plan will be executed by launching dedicated subagents. Every subagent must, upon completing its work, launch a **reviewer subagent** that validates the output against the plan requirements. The parent agent only accepts the work when the reviewer approves.
   343	
   344	### Subagent Launch Pattern
   345	```
   346	Parent Agent (Plan Phase N)
   347	  ├─ Worker Subagent
   348	  │    └─ Implements files, runs tests, verifies `npm run check`
   349	  └─ Reviewer Subagent (launched after Worker finishes)
   350	       └─ Reads diff, verifies requirements met, checks for regressions
   351	            ├─ PASS → Parent accepts, proceeds to Phase N+1
   352	            └─ FAIL → Parent sends feedback to Worker, retry
   353	```
   354

   356	1. All new files created match the plan specification
   357	2. `npm run check` passes with zero errors
   358	3. `npm run lint` shows no new errors (and ideally fewer than before)
   359	4. Existing functionality is preserved (tRPC endpoints respond, pipeline runs)
   360	5. No new `db` imports introduced outside repositories
   361	6. No SP-API references added
   362	
   363	---
   364	
   365	## Rollback & Safety Strategy
   366	
   367	- **Feature flags:** Each phase is gated by a commit. No phase requires deleting the old code until the next phase validates.
   368	- **Dual-write period (Phase 1–2):** SQLite and PostgreSQL run in parallel. Reads come from SQLite; writes go to both. After validation, switch reads to PostgreSQL.
   369	- **Type safety:** `npm run check` must pass before any phase is considered complete.

## Approved Plan:
# Optimus Rufus — Upgrade & Structural Optimization Plan

## Goal
Eliminate the architectural chokepoints identified by the knowledge graph (`db` god node, 154 cross-community links, 290 orphaned nodes) while migrating from ephemeral SQLite to persistent PostgreSQL + Drizzle ORM. **Remove Amazon SP-API dependency entirely** — it is undocumented in the active codebase and causes integration friction. **Restructure the AI pipeline so every agent execution is followed by an evaluator subagent review**.

## Approach
Incremental refactoring in 7 phases. Each phase is designed to be committable independently, with the app remaining functional after every phase. No big-bang rewrites. During plan execution, each phase will be delegated to a subagent, and each subagent will spawn a reviewer subagent to validate its output before the parent agent accepts the work.

## Key Architectural Decisions

### 1. No Amazon SP-API
- Remove all SP-API references from documentation, env vars, and architecture
- Primary data sources: **Apify scraper** + **Rainforest API** (already implemented)
- Listing enrichment via LLM-based inference rather than seller central APIs

### 2. Subagent Evaluation Pattern
Every pipeline stage will follow an **Execute → Evaluate → (Retry if needed)** loop:

```
StageExecutor
  ├─ ExecutionSubagent (does the work)
  └─ EvaluationSubagent (reviews the output)
       ├─ PASS → stage completes
       └─ FAIL → ExecutionSubagent retries with feedback
```

- Each `StageExecutor` delegates to an `ExecutionSubagent` class
- Each `ExecutionSubagent` has a paired `EvaluationSubagent` class
- The evaluator checks output quality, completeness, and schema validity
- After 3 failed evaluations, the stage fails with accumulated feedback
- This replaces the current monolithic `ReviewerAgent` with per-stage evaluators

---

**Why first:** Everything else depends on the database layer. The graph shows `db` has the highest betweenness centrality (0.036) and `client.ts` is the #1 node by degree (39).

### 1.1 Add Dependencies

npm install -D drizzle-kit @types/pg
```

### 1.2 Create Schema-as-Code
- Create `api/db/schema.ts` (new) using Drizzle's `pgTable` definitions
- Map all existing SQLite tables to PostgreSQL equivalents
- Use `serial`, `text`, `integer`, `real`, `timestamp`, `jsonb` appropriately
- Replace `JSON.stringify` fields with `jsonb` columns (gaps, topIssues, strengths, etc.)
- Keep `embeddingVector` as `text` for now (migrate to `vector` extension later)

### 1.3 Create Connection Layer
- `api/db/client.ts` → keep for backward compat during transition
- Create `api/db/drizzle.ts`: exports `drizzle(pool)` instance
- Create `api/db/migrate.ts`: runs Drizzle migrations via `drizzle-kit migrate`
- Environment: `DATABASE_URL` (PostgreSQL connection string)

### 1.4 Remove SP-API Artifacts
- Delete `docs/02-research/amazon-sp-api.md` if it exists

    // 50 lines of business logic ...

});

// After: router is a thin adapter

});
```

## Phase 5: Pipeline Decoupling + Subagent Evaluator Architecture

**Why:** `stages.ts` (degree 34, 16 cross-community) imports 7 agent classes, `db`, `copywriter`, `rufusSimulator`, `logger`, and `eventBus`. It is the #2 bridge node. We also must implement the **Execute → Evaluate → Retry** pattern for every stage.

### 5.1 Split `stages.ts` Into Three Files

**`api/pipeline/types.ts`** (already exists, but clean up):
- Keep `StageName`, `StageDefinition`, `StageOutput`, `PipelineJob`, `StageContext`, `StageExecutor`
- **Remove** the import from `../agents/types.js` — replace agent-specific types with generic `unknown` or define minimal pipeline-local interfaces

**`api/pipeline/definitions.ts`** (new):
- Only exports `STAGE_ORDER` — pure data, zero imports
```typescript
export const STAGE_ORDER: StageDefinition[] = [
  { name: "fetch", dependencies: [] },
  { name: "preprocess", dependencies: ["fetch"] },
  // ...
];
```

**`api/pipeline/executors.ts`** (new):
- Contains the `stageExecutors` array
- Imports agents, evaluators, services
- This is the only file that knows how to run stages

### 5.2 Implement Subagent Evaluator Pattern

Create `api/agents/evaluators/` with one evaluator per execution agent:

| Executor | Evaluator | Checks |
|---|---|---|
| `ApifyFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | ASIN data completeness, required fields present, schema valid |
| `ListingFetcherAgent` | `FetchEvaluator` | Same as above |
| `PreprocessorAgent` | `PreprocessEvaluator` | Text cleaned, no HTML artifacts, structure preserved |
| `EmbeddingGeneratorAgent` | `EmbeddingEvaluator` | Vector length correct (1536), no NaN values, normalized |
| `SemanticAnalyzerAgent` | `SemanticEvaluator` | Gap scores in [0,1], priorities valid, recommendations non-empty |
| `ContentOptimizerAgent` | `OptimizeEvaluator` | Title < 200 chars, 5 bullets, description valid HTML, QAs have answers |
| `CompetitorAnalystAgent` | `CompetitorEvaluator` | Competitor count > 0, scores in range, ASINs valid |

**Evaluator interface:**
```typescript
export interface Evaluator<T> {
  evaluate(input: unknown, output: T): Promise<{
    passed: boolean;
    score: number; // 0-100
    issues: string[];
    suggestions: string[];
  }>;
}
```

**Stage executor loop:**
```typescript
async function executeWithEvaluation<T>(
  executor: () => Promise<T>,
  evaluator: Evaluator<T>,
  input: unknown,
  maxAttempts = 3
): Promise<T> {
  for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxAttempts; attempt++) {
    const output = await executor();
    const review = await evaluator.evaluate(input, output);
    if (review.passed) return output;
    if (attempt === maxAttempts) {
      throw new Error(`Stage failed evaluation after ${maxAttempts} attempts: ${review.issues.join("; ")}`);
    }
    // Log feedback for retry
    logger.warn("Stage evaluation failed, retrying", { attempt, issues: review.issues });
  }
  throw new Error("Unreachable");
}
```

**Note:** The current `ReviewerAgent` is a generic post-hoc reviewer. The new evaluators are **per-stage, schema-aware, and triggered automatically** within the pipeline loop. `ReviewerAgent` can be deleted or repurposed as a final quality gate after all stages complete.

### 5.3 Remove `db` Access from Stage Executors
- The `embedding` stage currently does: `db.prepare("UPDATE listings SET embeddingVector ...")`
- Move this to `listingService.updateEmbedding()`
- The `optimize` stage currently does: `db.prepare("SELECT firstName, lastName ...")`
- Move this to `prospectService.getForPipeline(ctx.prospectId)`

### 5.4 Target State
- `engine.ts` only imports `STAGE_ORDER` from `definitions.ts` and `stageExecutors` from `executors.ts`
- `definitions.ts` has **zero** cross-community links
- `engine.ts` degree drops from 22 to ~12
- Each stage has a dedicated evaluator in `api/agents/evaluators/`
- Pipeline failures include specific evaluator feedback in the error log

## Execution Model: Subagent Delegation

Each phase of this plan will be executed by launching dedicated subagents. Every subagent must, upon completing its work, launch a **reviewer subagent** that validates the output against the plan requirements. The parent agent only accepts the work when the reviewer approves.

### Subagent Launch Pattern
```
Parent Agent (Plan Phase N)
  ├─ Worker Subagent
  │    └─ Implements files, runs tests, verifies `npm run check`
  └─ Reviewer Subagent (launched after Worker finishes)
       └─ Reads diff, verifies requirements met, checks for regressions
            ├─ PASS → Parent accepts, proceeds to Phase N+1
            └─ FAIL → Parent sends feedback to Worker, retry
```

### Reviewer Persona: Grumpy Senior Engineer
The reviewer subagent **must** act like a senior staff engineer who:
- Has been woken up at 3 AM by a production outage caused by sloppy code
- Treats every PR like it might be the one that crashes the cluster
- Questions **everything**: naming, edge cases, error handling, type safety, performance
- Asks "What happens when this fails?" for every async call
- Rejects code for vague variable names, missing `try/catch`, or `any` types
- Demands proof: "Show me the test. Show me the type check. Show me the error path."
- **Zero tolerance** for:
  - `console.log` instead of structured logging
  - Raw SQL outside repositories
  - Missing return types on exported functions
  - `any` or `unknown` without justification
  - Functions over 50 lines without a comment explaining why
  - Dependencies added without a reason
  - "It works on my machine" energy

### Reviewer Checklist (per phase)
1. All new files created match the plan specification
2. `npm run check` passes with zero errors
3. `npm run lint` shows no new errors (and ideally fewer than before)
4. Existing functionality is preserved (tRPC endpoints respond, pipeline runs)
5. No new `db` imports introduced outside repositories
6. No SP-API references added
7. **Every exported function has an explicit return type**
8. **Every `await` is inside a `try/catch` or the function declares `throws`**
9. **No `any` types unless accompanied by a 1-line comment explaining the escape hatch**
10. **No function over 40 lines without being split or heavily commented**
11. **Error messages are actionable** (not "something went wrong")

---

## Rollback & Safety Strategy

- **Feature flags:** Each phase is gated by a commit. No phase requires deleting the old code until the next phase validates.
- **Dual-write period (Phase 1–2):** SQLite and PostgreSQL run in parallel. Reads come from SQLite; writes go to both. After validation, switch reads to PostgreSQL.
- **Type safety:** `npm run check` must pass before any phase is considered complete.

---

## Estimated Effort

| Phase | Files Touched | Estimated Time | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1. Drizzle + PostgreSQL | 4 new, 1 modified | 4–6 hours | Medium |
| 2. Repository Layer | 9 new, ~15 modified | 6–8 hours | Low |
| 3. Extract Types | 2 new, ~20 modified | 2–3 hours | Low |
| 4. Service Layer | 5 new, ~10 modified | 4–6 hours | Low |
| 5. Pipeline Decoupling + Evaluators | 9 new, 3 modified | 5–7 hours | Medium |
| 6. Frontend Cleanup | 3 new, 1 modified | 2–3 hours | Low |
| 7. Auth + Quality + Tests | 5 new, ~10 modified | 6–8 hours | Medium |
| **Total** | **~30 new, ~60 modified** | **27–38 hours** | **Managed** |

---

- `db` node degree < 5

### 5. Design Decisions & Notes
- **Kept `api/db/client.ts`** (SQLite) untouched for backward compatibility as required.
- **Did not modify any routers or pipeline code** — all existing tRPC routers remain intact.
- **`jobs.id` uses `text("id").primaryKey()`** instead of `serial` because `api/infra/queue.ts` inserts string IDs (`${Date.now()}-${...}`). All other tables use `serial("id").primaryKey()`.
- **JSON fields** (bullets, images, rawScrapeData, gaps, topIssues, strengths, opportunities, asinRankings, stagesJSON, outputJSON, eventData, simulatorScenarios, transformBefore, transformAfter, dataJSON, optsJSON, stacktraceJSON) all migrated to `jsonb()`.
- **Migration script** handles JSON serialization via `safeJsonParse`, converts SQLite datetime strings to `Date` objects, preserves original integer IDs, and resets PostgreSQL sequences after insert so `serial` continues from the max migrated value.
- **Foreign key `onDelete` behaviors** preserved to match existing SQLite schema (cascade/set null where applicable).

- **None.** All checks pass. No new lint errors. Ready for Phase 2.

import {
  pgTable,
  serial,
  text,
  integer,
  real,
  timestamp,
  jsonb,
  bigint,
} from "drizzle-orm/pg-core";

export const prospects = pgTable("prospects", {
  id: serial("id").primaryKey(),
  slug: text("slug").notNull().unique(),
  email: text("email").notNull(),
  firstName: text("first_name"),
  lastName: text("last_name"),
  company: text("company"),
  apolloContactId: text("apollo_contact_id"),
  apolloSequenceId: text("apollo_sequence_id"),
  status: text("status").default("new"),
  landingPageViews: integer("landing_page_views").default(0),
  packageType: text("package_type").default("package_2"),
  pricePoint: real("price_point").default(1500),
  createdAt: timestamp("created_at", { withTimezone: true }).defaultNow(),
});

export const listings = pgTable("listings", {
  id: serial("id").primaryKey(),

/**
 * SQLite → PostgreSQL data migration script.
 *
 * Reads from the existing SQLite database (via api/db/client.ts)
 * and writes to PostgreSQL via Drizzle ORM.
 *
 * Run with:
 *   DATABASE_URL=postgres://... npx tsx scripts/migrateSqliteToPostgres.ts
 */

import { drizzle } from "drizzle-orm/node-postgres";
import { Pool } from "pg";
import { db as sqliteDb } from "../api/db/client.js";
import * as schema from "../api/db/schema.js";

const pool = new Pool({
  connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL,
});

const pgDb = drizzle(pool, { schema });

/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */
// Helpers
/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */

function safeJsonParse<T>(value: unknown): T | null {
  if (value === null || value === undefined) return null;
  if (typeof value === "object") return value as T;
  try {
    return JSON.parse(String(value)) as T;
  } catch {
    return null;
  }
}

function toDate(value: unknown): Date | null {
  if (value === null || value === undefined) return null;
  const d = new Date(String(value));
  return isNaN(d.getTime()) ? null : d;
}

function toText(value: unknown): string | null {
  if (value === null || value === undefined) return null;
  return String(value);
}

function toNumber(value: unknown): number | null {
  if (value === null || value === undefined) return null;
  const n = Number(value);
  return isNaN(n) ? null : n;
}

function toInteger(value: unknown): number | null {
  if (value === null || value === undefined) return null;
  const n = Number(value);
  return isNaN(n) ? null : Math.floor(n);
}

/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */
// Table migrations (in dependency order)
/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */

async function migrateProspects(): Promise<void> {
  console.log("📦 Migrating prospects...");
  const rows = sqliteDb
    .prepare("SELECT * FROM prospects")
    .all() as Record<string, unknown>[];
  if (rows.length === 0) {
    console.log("   → no rows");
    return;
  }

  const values = rows.map((r) => ({
    id: toInteger(r.id)!,
    slug: toText(r.slug)!,
    email: toText(r.email)!,
    firstName: toText(r.firstName),
    lastName: toText(r.lastName),
    company: toText(r.company),
    apolloContactId: toText(r.apolloContactId),


</details>
